Clash Between Pseudo-Troops in Heilongjiang and Outer Mongolian Troops

Contact Between Both Sides Near Lake Baikal: One Pseudo-Military Officer and One Soldier Killed 5

(Changchun) According to Japanese and puppet statements, on January 8, Outer Mongolian and Russian troops occupied the puppet side's fishing ground in Lake Baikal. On January 9, Russian troops occupied the triangular area where the three rivers north of the lake meet. On January 24, Major Honda, an instructor of the puppet army, led eleven Japanese and puppet troops to investigate the triangular area. Suddenly, at noon on the same day, they were attacked by Russian troops. Instructor Lieutenant Seno and one non-commissioned officer and one soldier were killed. According to another source, because Japanese and puppet reinforcements arrived, the two sides are still fighting fiercely. The Japanese and puppet troops are determined to fight the Russian troops and have mobilized all the troops stationed in Kouping Lunbell to concentrate on Lake Baikal. (25th China United News Agency Telegram)

(Harbin) According to sources, at noon yesterday, the puppet troops stationed on the border between Heilongjiang and Outer Mongolia clashed with the Russian Red Army. The puppet troops suffered heavy casualties. The location of the clash was near Lake Baikal. (25th China United News Agency Telegram)

(Changchun) According to a telegram from Hailar, "Manchukuo" troops clashed with Outer Mongolian troops on the 24th while conducting reconnaissance near the Halha Temple north of Lake Baikal. The commander of the Manchu army, Seo, and one soldier were killed, and several soldiers were injured. (24th Japan Associated Press Telegram)

(Tokyo) According to Japanese sources in Changchun, Outer Mongolian troops invaded the territory of Manchukuo and attacked the "Man" army. "When a team of 'Man' army was patrolling near the Halha Temple north of Lake Baikal yesterday afternoon, Outer Mongolian troops suddenly launched an attack. The 'Man' army was unprepared and suffered many casualties. Details are still unknown. Some here expect a serious development. However, this matter is not related to the dispute on the Chahar border. It is heard that the 'Man' army counterattacked yesterday afternoon, but the situation is unknown. Whether this matter will escalate is still questionable. According to the Japan-'Man' Agreement, Japan is responsible for protecting the territory of Manchukuo. Some say that if Outer Mongolia sends troops to assist and expands the scope of the matter, Japan will inevitably intervene. However, those in charge do not believe in spreading rumors. (25th Reuters Telegram)

Pseudo-Troops Outside Xinglong Bianqiang Confiscate Civilian Guns 6

(Tianjin) The puppet Jehol army is forcibly collecting taxes and confiscating civilian guns in the area outside Xinglong Bianqiang, saying that each big gun is priced at 15 yuan, but after they are confiscated, they do not pay. Now they are also implementing conscription, 30 people from big villages and 5 people from small villages, causing residents to panic and flee to Malanyu. (25th Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Banbishan in the third district of Zunhua was occupied by the puppet side after the incident. On the 21st, the puppet army confiscated firearms in the area, leading to a battle. The puppet army was driven into the valley, and 20 firearms were seized. On the 23rd, the Japanese army from Saheqiao rushed to assist. Nearby residents fled to the Luowenyu area. The Zunhua County Government ordered the public security bureaus in each district to properly settle the refugees fleeing from outside the mouth. Those carrying weapons were ordered to register to avoid misunderstandings. (25th Dispatch)

Military Attaché Kageza Arrives in Nanjing for Secret Talks with the Japanese Consul General 7

(Nanjing) Lieutenant Colonel Kageza, the military attaché stationed in Shanghai, arrived here from Shanghai this morning. He immediately went to the consulate general to have a three-way secret discussion with Consul General Suma and military attaché Amemiya for several hours. Although the content of the secret discussion is unknown, it seems that they are planning a fairly important matter. (25th Dentsu News Agency Telegram)

Japanese Troops in Tianjin Hold Street Fighting Exercises 8

(Tianjin) More than 500 Japanese infantry and artillery troops in Tianjin, under the command of Regiment Commander Morimoto, conducted street fighting exercises in the Japanese concession's Fushimi, Naniwa, Miyajima, and Matsushima streets at 1 p.m. today, and piled sandbags and laid electric nets on Kasuga, Fuyong, Naniwa, and Fushimi streets to cut off traffic. The first part of the troops erected cannons on the roof of the Zhongyuan Company building and simulated shooting at the Chinese territory in Hebei. Commander Umezu and Chief of Staff Sakai Takashi and others came and went to give instructions. The exercises ended at 4 p.m. (25th Dispatch)

Hebei Provincial Government to Move to Baoding Next Month 9

(Beiping) Yu Xuezhong has appointed Deputy Chief of Staff Jiang Chunyan to go to Baoding to survey the government site. The repair project of the Baoding government site can begin next month. Yu has decided to move within next month. The provincial government will work in Baoding from March 1. (25th Dispatch) (Beiping) The move of the Hebei Provincial Government to Baoding was temporarily difficult to realize because the address had not yet been arranged. The Provincial Government has now sent personnel to arrange it, and it can be moved in about early March. (25th Central News Agency Telegram)

(Tianjin) The reorganization plan for the Hebei Civil Affairs Department was passed at today's provincial government regular meeting. The police department will be incorporated, and four sections will be set up. (25th Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Yu Xuezhong talked about: (1) The houses for the provincial government's move to Baoding have been found, about a hundred rooms. Although it is not enough, it can be used. The repair work could not start before because of the winter cold. Now it is planned to send people to inspect and repair it immediately. (2) The joint office plan for the provincial government has been planned and will be implemented before the move to Baoding. (3) There are not many remnants of Liu Guitang's troops, and they are causing trouble in Zunhua County. The county's local troops are capable of dealing with it and will not cause trouble. (25th Dispatch)

The Yutian Local Troops Have Not Been Able to Be Reorganized Temporarily 10

(Tianjin) Yu Xuezhong talked about: The reorganization of the Yutian Security Team and the local militia has been suspended due to the Chahar incident. The Security Team has not taken any action recently. Wang Bingxiao's troops have retreated to the border between Yutian and Jizhou. The Security Team currently has more than 2,000 people, which is more than double the number stipulated. Chief Sun Jizhou's actions are not free. Every time he sends a telegram, it is not of his own volition. Among them, Feng Shoupeng's troops have the worst discipline, and local ruffians take the opportunity to flaunt their names, causing outsiders to mistakenly believe that they cannot be cleaned up. (25th Dispatch)

(Beiping) After the conflict between Wang Bingxiao's troops in the Yutian militia and Feng Pengshou's troops in the Security Team, Wang's troops have now retreated to the area of ​​large and small Tuancheng and merged with Li Jizhou's troops in the militia, with a force of about seven or eight hundred people and complete firearms. The area of ​​large and small Tuancheng has been surrounded by the Security Team. Wang's troops are attempting to break through and are contacting other militia forces to attack the Security Team. The Jizhou-Miyun District Office has ordered all counties to strictly guard against it. (25th Dispatch)

Italian Ambassador's Audience with Chairman Lin 11

Presentation of Credentials Ceremony Grand

Chairman Lin Hosts a Lavish Banquet

(Nanjing) Italian Ambassador, Mr. Lo Jacono, accompanied by First Secretary Mr. Gabassi, Secretary Marquis Qi Daiting, Consul and Translator Mr. Ross, Chinese Secretary Mr. Fei Yangyue, Air Force Attache Mr. De Laigu, and Naval Attache Mr. Spaccogna, proceeded to the National Government at 11:30 AM on the 25th to have an audience with Chairman Lin and present their credentials. Prior to this, the National Government dispatched Military Counselor Mao Zhongfang and Chief of Section Liu Naifan of the Bureau of Ceremonies, dressed in ceremonial attire, to the Ambassador's residence in Tieguan Lane, Shigulu, by official and deputy limousines. Extra guards were stationed along the route, and military police saluted as the Ambassador's motorcade passed. On that day, two rows of guards were stationed inside the main gate of the National Government, impeccably dressed, to welcome the delegation. After the Ambassador and his entourage arrived in the limousines, they were directed by a senior officer of the guards, who sounded a bugle salute as the Ambassador's motorcade passed, and the officer performed a saber salute. Section Chief Li Youzheng of the Bureau of Ceremonies of the National Government and Section Chief Lin Tongshi of the External Affairs Section of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs greeted them at the entrance of the main hall and led them inside on foot. A military band was stationed inside the main hall, and they played the Italian national anthem as the Ambassador passed as a welcome. The Ambassador and his party stopped to return the salute, and then proceeded to the reception room. Chief Military Counselor Lu Chao greeted them at the foot of the steps and led them into the room to rest. Section Chief Lin of the External Affairs Section of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and Section Chief Li of the Bureau of Ceremonies jointly provided hospitality. After the Ambassador arrived at the National Government, Section Chief Liu of the Bureau of Ceremonies entered to inform Chairman Lin, who then emerged into the ceremonial hall and stood in the center. Chief Civil Secretary Wei Huai led all the secretaries, and Chief Military Counselor Lu Chao led all the military counselors, civil officials on the east and military officials on the west, lined up in order on both sides. Vice Minister Xu Mo and translation staff from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs stood to the right of the Chairman. Once the arrangements were complete, Section Chief Liu of the Bureau of Ceremonies invited the Ambassador to the audience. Section Chief Liu guided the Ambassador into the ceremonial hall, where the Ambassador bowed once to the Chairman, then bowed again in the center of the hall, and bowed once more before the Chairman. The Chairman returned each bow. The Ambassador stood still and delivered his speech, after which a designated translator stepped forward from the ranks and translated it into Chinese for the Chairman. After the translation, the Ambassador stepped forward to present his credentials and returned to his original position. The Chairman accepted the credentials and handed them over to Vice Minister Xu Mo. Then, the Chairman read his reply, which was translated by a designated translator from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. After the translation, the Ambassador stepped forward, and the Chairman shook hands and conversed with the Ambassador, with the translator stepping forward to convey the message. The Chairman first inquired about the health of the Italian monarch. After a brief exchange, the Ambassador introduced the members of his delegation, and the Chairman shook hands with each of them. The Chairman then shook hands with the Ambassador again. The Ambassador stood at attention, bowed once to the Chairman, and stepped backward, bowing again. He then bowed once more in the center of the hall. The Chairman returned each bow. The Ambassador and his delegation exited the ceremonial hall and were led by Section Chief Liu of the Bureau of Ceremonies into the reception room. Vice Minister Xu Mo, Chief Civil Secretary Wei Huai, and Chief Military Counselor Lu Chao simultaneously entered the reception room to engage with the Ambassador. The Chairman returned to his office to rest.

▲ Text of the Credentials: The translated text of the credentials presented by Italian Ambassador Lo Jacono is as follows: Your Excellency, Mr. Chairman, I have been appointed by my monarch as the Ambassador Extraordinary and Plenipotentiary to the Republic of China, succeeding Minister Pusterla. It is with great honor that I personally present my credentials to your great Chairman. In ancient times, when other human civilizations were still in their infancy, our two great cultures of the East and West were already shining brightly throughout the world. To bridge the two continents, the Eurasian route across the Black Sea and the majestic mountains, which we call the "Avenue of the Genovese," stands as a testament in world history to the dedication of Italians in connecting East and West. I am deeply proud to take up my new post today as the first Italian Ambassador to China in this spirit. This mission aligns with the objectives of all endeavors of the Italian government, envisioning the future based on past plans. Italy, under the guidance of a great leader, has been revitalized through a spiritual reformation. This coincides with the same movement and similar aspirations of your nation's leaders, who are concentrating their efforts on the construction of a new China. Therefore, the cooperation between our two nations is gradually developing with mutual relevance in history. I firmly believe that the government of the Great Republic of China will value the friendly policy of Italy towards China, as its policy is neither biased nor does it serve any other purpose. I sincerely hope that I will receive your Excellency's favor and assistance in performing my duties, and I also wish for the support of all the wise men currently leading China towards a glorious future. This is what I aspire to.

▲ Chairman's Reply: The reply of Chairman Lin to Ambassador Lo Jacono upon receiving his credentials is as follows: Your Excellency, Mr. Ambassador, I am pleased to receive the letter of credence you have personally delivered today, by order of Your Great Monarch, as well as the letter of recall from the previous Minister Pusterla. I am greatly pleased to hear of the friendly policy of your government toward China, and the National Government will reciprocate with the same friendship towards Italy. The people of your nation, with their courageous and steadfast spirit, have bridged the two great cultures of the East and West. Centuries ago, they fostered mutual admiration between our two peoples. Today, your nation is undergoing a spiritual reformation and revitalization under the guidance of an enlightened leader. We, likewise, are making similar efforts in the construction of a new China. The cooperation between China and Italy will surely lead to a bright and prosperous future. I extend a special welcome to you as the first Italian Ambassador to be stationed in our country and will provide my assistance so that you may fulfill your great mission. (Central News Agency dispatch, 25th)

(Nanjing) At 12:30 PM, Chairman Lin hosted a banquet at the National Government, featuring exquisite Chinese cuisine, to entertain Ambassador Lo Jacono and his accompanying delegation. Wang Zhaoming, Sun Ke, Chen Tiaoyuan, Shao Yuanchong, Ding Weifen, Xu Mo, and others were in attendance. When all the guests were present, Chief Military Counselor Lu Chao entered to inform the Chairman, who then proceeded to the reception room. Section Chief Liu of the Bureau of Ceremonies invited the guests to be seated. The Chairman invited the Ambassador to walk with him to the reception room to be seated. The other guests followed suit in order. The banquet concluded at 2:00 PM. Section Chief Liu of the Bureau of Ceremonies invited the Chairman, the Ambassador, and the guests to take a photograph in front of the corridor. They then returned to the reception room for tea and cigarettes. The Chairman first shook hands with the Ambassador to bid farewell and returned to his office. When the Ambassador took his leave, the Minister of Foreign Affairs escorted him to the entrance of the reception room, while the Chief Civil Secretary and the Chief Military Counselor escorted him to the foot of the stairs. Section Chief Liu of the Bureau of Ceremonies and Section Chief Lin of the External Affairs Section of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs escorted him to the door of the main hall where the limousines were waiting. Military Counselor Mao Zhongfang and Section Chief Liu Naifan then accompanied Ambassador Lo Jacono and his delegation back to the Embassy in their respective limousines for rest. (Central News Agency dispatch, 25th)

(Nanjing) At 4:00 PM on the 25th, President Wang, accompanied by Section Chief Lin Tongshi of the External Affairs Section of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and translator Wang Suizheng, traveled by car to the Italian Embassy to return the visit. The Italian Ambassador, along with his staff, personally greeted them and invited them into the reception room for a brief discussion. Wang then departed. At 4:30 PM, Chief Military Counselor Lu Chao of the National Government, accompanied by Section Chief Liu Naifan of the Bureau of Ceremonies, presented Chairman Lin's visiting card and visited the foreign embassy on his behalf. The Italian Ambassador and others personally greeted them and welcomed them into the reception room, where they sat and chatted for a short while before Lu and his party took their leave and returned to the National Government. At 8:00 PM, Wang hosted a banquet at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for the Italian Ambassador and his wife, as well as their staff. Presidents and ministers of various Yuan and Ministries, directors of various departments of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, counselors, secretaries, and others were in attendance. The atmosphere was lively with toasts and conversation. The gathering dispersed at approximately 10:00 PM. The Italian Ambassador is scheduled to pay respects at Dr. Sun Yat-Sen's Mausoleum on the morning of the 26th and lay a wreath. He is also scheduled to hold a tea party at the Italian Embassy from 5:00 PM to 7:00 PM on the afternoon of the 26th to entertain the presidents and ministers of various Yuan and Ministries of our country. (Central News Agency dispatch, 25th)

Current Commentary

The Chahar Eastern Region Issue 16

Since the 20th of this month, the Chahar eastern region has suddenly been attacked by Japanese puppet troops, with infantry and cavalry advancing in all directions, and aircraft bombing. Detailed reports and accurate statistics are currently difficult to obtain. However, the unprovoked aggression of the Japanese puppet troops is a fact. Unexpectedly, Japanese newspapers such as the Tokyo Nichi Nichi Shimbun have described this event as an invasion of the Jehol border by Chinese troops, claiming that the Japanese army's actions were for self-defense. Today, the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs, based on a report from the Kwantung Army, sent instructions to its overseas embassies, propagating this narrative and placing responsibility on the Chinese army. If they adopt this line to deal with this issue, not only will the various problems between China and Japan since the September 18th Incident be difficult to resolve, but also all international justice will be impossible to maintain.

Since the Zhangjiakou Incident last year, the Chinese government has made every effort to maintain peace, and its diplomatic policy towards Japan has strived to minimize and resolve all issues. This is known to the world. Even regarding eastern Chahar, the facts are not only different from what the Japanese have claimed, but also, after the dispersal of Liu Guitang's troops and the westward relocation of Zhang Yunrong's troops from Shangdu, China has not stationed any troops there. How could there be any disturbance of the Jehol border? The Japanese authorities should be aware of this situation. Is it possible that the Tokyo Nichi Nichi Shimbun, which pays great attention to peace relations in the Far East, is unaware of this? This is what the Chinese people should first declare.

Recently, the external propaganda and diplomatic movements within Japan have shown a tendency to gradually return to normalcy. It is making efforts to show goodwill towards the United States, maintaining a serious attitude towards the Soviet Union, and also seeking understanding with the United Kingdom. Although its attitude towards China is not entirely clear, it also seems to have a peaceful inclination. The possibility of re-establishing peaceful relations in East Asia may temporarily exist. During this period, even if there are misunderstandings with the Chinese troops in eastern Chahar, they should be resolved through diplomatic channels. Now, while the diplomatic authorities are declaring friendship, the military is acting independently. This will not only make future efforts at friendship impossible, but also render all previous efforts futile. This is what Japanese intellectuals deeply regret.

When the Preparatory Conference for the Naval Disarmament Treaty reached an impasse at the end of last year, the international situation temporarily became perilous. However, since the Franco-Italian understanding was reached at the beginning of this month, and the United States joined the International Court of Justice, and the Saar plebiscite results were announced, the atmosphere of world peace has become stronger again. Consequently, the naval reduction issue among Britain, the United States, and Japan will also be influenced by the peaceful atmosphere. In the near future, a naval arms race is unlikely to occur. However, the relationship between China and Japan is a crucial key to the Far Eastern issue. If it is not handled appropriately, it could impede the progress of peace between the two countries, or even jeopardize the global peace situation. Therefore, China's forbearance and restraint are solely for the sake of international relations and the responsibility of maintaining world peace. Japan should calmly study this matter and avoid self-deception through embellishment. Moreover, the area of eastern Chahar was originally very peaceful. After several bombings, China remains calm. The rights and wrongs are very clear. Therefore, the Japanese diplomatic community is already aware that this matter should not be escalated. Even the military attache stationed in Japan believes that it will not lead to a major crisis. Therefore, the future of this issue depends entirely on Japan's proper handling of it.

China has made every effort for peace and has not hesitated to pay a high price for peace. If it still cannot obtain a peaceful understanding, it knows where the responsibility lies and how to protect itself. Currently, China's economy and military may lag behind other nations. However, the loyalty of its people to the country may not be inferior to that of advanced nations. Japan shares the same writing system as China and has a deep historical and cultural connection. It should know that the Chinese nation is by no means a lazy nation. If Japan truly wants to maintain peace in the Far East, it should not rely on military force as a panacea and disregard everything else.

Philippine Governor-General Passes Through Hong Kong on Return to the United States 17

Optimistic About the Future of Independence

(Hong Kong) Governor-General Murphy, who went to the United States to confer with President Roosevelt on the issue of Philippine independence, passed through here today on the President Hoover. He was accompanied by Quezon, the Speaker of the Philippine Senate and future President of the Republic. Quezon will return to Manila on the President Grant. The US Consul General Hoover and a representative of Hong Kong Governor Peel boarded the ship to welcome them. Murphy said that since departing from Manila, he and Quezon had discussed the Philippine constitution at length, focusing particularly on the procedures for obtaining US approval under the law and other steps for organizing the republican government. He did not touch upon amending the Philippine Independence Act. Murphy expressed optimism about the future of the Philippine Republican government, stating that they are fully prepared to rebuild the republican government, and the Philippine people have long awaited it. The republican government will certainly succeed. (National Telegram, 25th)

US Position on the World Court 18

Senate Still Has Opposition

(Washington) Those in the Senate opposed to the United States joining the World Court are still struggling today, while government leaders are planning to find a way to vote on the case as soon as possible. The opposition attempted a compromise when the Senate passed a reservation proposed by Republican Senator Vandenberg that other countries cannot interfere in US internal affairs. Reynolds still claims that joining the World Court is a shortcut for the United States to join the League of Nations. Reynolds also stated that only France and Italy have benefited in the League of Nations, as in the recent Franco-Italian understanding on North African territories. However, for China, the League of Nations is at a loss for solutions. Afterward, an Associated Press reporter interviewed Reynolds, and he reiterated his previous statement, adding that Japan is planning to seize Australia within fifty years. He said, "Japan is doing whatever it wants in China, first invading Manchuria, and now reaching Mongolia. At that time, the League of Nations handed over the German-owned islands in the Pacific to Japan for trusteeship, which has brought them closer to Australia by thousands of miles. And Australia is Japan's only backdoor." (National Telegram, 24th)

Roosevelt Asks Congress to Allocate Huge Sums 19

To Develop Natural Resources

Public Works Bill Passed by the House

Requires $480 Million

(Washington) The House of Representatives today passed the government's $4,880,000,000 relief bill by a vote of 328 to 78. During the debate, the government派 (faction) struck down various amendments. The bill has now been sent to the Senate. (Reuters, 24th)

(Washington) President Roosevelt today sent a special message to Congress, proposing to allocate tens of thousands of millions of US dollars to preserve and develop the nation's natural resources. After the message was read, the House immediately passed the Public Works Relief Bill, which requires $480,000,000. The President's message stated that the nation's natural resources, such as land, timber, minerals, water, etc., urgently need to stop the careless waste. At the same time, the National Resources Committee also presented a long-term plan to develop public works over the next twenty years, requiring approximately $500 million annually, totaling $100,000 million. President Roosevelt said that a large part of the $480 million in the Public Works Relief Bill could be used for the National Resources Committee, saying, "Once the current unemployment crisis has improved slightly, we can allocate another $500 million annually." The committee has also suggested plans to control floods, prevent soil erosion, rebuild forests, and nationalize bituminous coal. (Si Min News, 24th)

American Economics Professor Criticizes Silver Purchase Policy 20

Chinese Financial Instability

Japan Also Affected

Montreal Professor 台 of economics at McGill University gave a speech here today, vehemently criticizing the US government's silver purchase policy, saying that the US is implementing Roosevelt's silver policy, buying up most of the world's silver reserves, but its purpose is unknown, merely causing countries around the world to seek another international price standard. If it continues to stubbornly follow its own path, the result will be that the United States absorbs most of the world's silver, the same as absorbing most of the world's gold. Gold can no longer be the standard of international value. China, the only silver-using country in the world, will now be forced to abandon the silver standard. Countries around the world will now have to use the pound sterling as the international price standard. (National Telegram, 24th)

(Washington) House Silverite leader Freshman declared today that the impact of rising silver prices on Chinese finance is only temporary. China is currently experiencing currency contraction, similar to the currency contraction in gold-using countries after the rise in gold prices. Corrective measures are now being taken to satisfy China. The fundamental way to alleviate the financial and economic difficulties of China and other countries lies in raising world prices. (National Telegram, 24th)

(Washington) China's strong opposition to the US silver purchase policy has prompted attention in Washington to Japan's reaction to the policy. Speculation has arisen regarding discussions between Japanese financial leaders and bankers from "Manchukuo" to place the exchange rate between the Japanese yen and the new silver yuan of "Manchukuo" on an equal footing. Experts in Washington do not believe that Japan will establish a fixed relationship between "Manchukuo's" silver yuan and the Japanese yen recently for two reasons: (1) Most of the people of "Manchukuo" are accustomed to using silver yuan. (2) Establishing a relationship between "Manchukuo's" silver yuan and the Japanese yen would cause "Manchukuo" to lose its independent form. However, this may be possible in the future after Japan controls "Manchukuo's" commerce and Japanese yen become commonly used in "Manchukuo", and the Japanese yen becomes the reserve currency of "Manchukuo's" banks. Congressional silverites once believed that Japan also supported raising silver prices because rising silver prices would increase the purchasing power of India and China. However, according to recent news from the East, the Japanese have realized that the rise in silver prices not only fails to increase China's purchasing power, but actually causes China to lose silver yuan, the only currency of transaction. Japan is also quite affected by the US silver purchase policy because rising silver prices disrupt China's commerce and finance. (National Telegram, 24th)

Former British Chancellor of the Exchequer Vigorously Condemns 21

Nationalization of Banks Plan

Supports Government's Currency Depreciation Policy

Says it Can Lead to Domestic Revival

(London) At the annual meeting of the Midland Bank today, Chairman McKenna (who served as Chancellor of the Exchequer in 1915) spoke out against the plan proposed by some to nationalize banks, and stated the dangers of the banking monopoly system and the convenience of the existing banking organization. McKenna praised the government's cheap money policy, saying that if this policy continues, it will definitely lead to domestic recovery. He also said that the gradual domestic recovery will inevitably absorb greater imports, but this will facilitate the payment of interest on overseas investments, so, in summary, the balance of payments remains unchanged. Today, as gold prices continue to fall, the value of the pound sterling remains stable.

This is the good effect of Britain abandoning the gold standard. Under the old system, the depreciation of the pound sterling would have required the implementation of contraction plans, which would have adversely affected commerce. But today, there is no need for contraction. In his personal opinion, he does not believe that the recovery of domestic businesses has reached its peak, because a large supply of labor has not yet been utilized, and many basic desires have not yet been satisfied. (Reuters, 24th)

Italian Cabinet Reshuffle 24

Seeking Rapid Development of the Corporatist System

All Policies Remain the Same

(Rome) The Italian cabinet has recently been reshuffled. In addition to Prime Minister Mussolini, who remains Minister of Interior, Foreign Affairs, Army, Navy, Air Force, Corporations, and Colonies, Finance Minister Junger has been replaced by Turin Provincial Governor Lival. Education Minister Egorel has been replaced by Ambassador to the Vatican Count Difursiber. Agriculture Minister Acebo has been replaced by Deputy Secretary of the Prime Minister's Office, Losani. Labor Minister DiCloralarange has been replaced by Lacha, the former representative to the International Labor Conference. Justice Minister Francis has been replaced by Sormi, the former Deputy Minister of Education. Count Xunibo has been appointed as Minister of Transportation, and three Deputy Ministers and the Prince Rudovici, Governor of Rome, have also been dismissed and reassigned. (Havas, 24th)

(Rome) Italian Prime Minister Mussolini reorganized the cabinet on schedule, replacing many current cabinet members with people who have assisted him in organizing the Corporate Council, which is the economic parliament of Italy. The purpose of the Italian Prime Minister seems to be to quickly develop the Italian corporatist system with their help. Rivar, the new Minister of Finance, was originally the Mayor of Turin. Mussolini, as before, remains in charge of seven ministries. Prince Peng Kebagni was appointed as a nominal state official today to reward his services. Potais has been appointed to fill the post of Governor of Rome, which he left behind. The Corporate Council is a revolutionary new type of parliament responsible for managing Italy's economic life. It has representatives from twenty-two fascist corporate bodies, including all departments of Italy's productive activities. Mussolini, as Prime Minister of the Ministry of Corporate Affairs and Prime Minister of each corporate body, each corporate body has representatives from both labor and management, as well as three fascist party members to monitor all political resolutions in the group. (Reuters, 24th)

Closer Centralization of German Political Power 25

Nation Divided into Twenty-Two Administrative Districts

Each District to Have a Governor Representing the Central Government

(Berlin) The National Socialist Party's plan to overhaul the current German political structure, long awaited, has taken another step forward with today's cabinet meeting. A new plan, modeled after the French system, divides the country into several administrative regions. Each region will be governed by a National Socialist administrator holding full administrative powers. Judicial authority in each state and province will be under the jurisdiction of the Minister of Justice. Today's cabinet meeting also considered legislation to reduce interest rates for banks and other lending institutions, viewing this as an important plan to assist industry and commerce and promote government projects. The plan is expected to be presented for discussion when the Reichstag reconvenes on the 30th of this month. (Reuters, 24th)

(Berlin) The government has promulgated laws to change the local system, concentrating local power in the central government. The German states are completely abolished and replaced by twenty-two large administrative regions. Prussia's twelve provinces are each divided into one region, while the remaining former states are divided into ten regions. Each region is headed by a governor, abolishing the former premiership system. The governor represents the central government and holds administrative power. Judicial power no longer belongs to the local level but to the central government. Furthermore, regulations within the reform law for rural towns and villages stipulate that the National Socialist Party can intervene in the administrative power of towns and villages. (Havas, 24th)

(Berlin) Regarding the reorganization of the National Socialist Party's armed forces, it is generally understood that it will be carried out according to the principles previously announced by Führer Hitler. That is, only the national defense forces within the Third Reich are allowed to be equipped with military arms. Although the Party's armed forces do not necessarily have to be regarded as ordinary citizens, all national military training must be centralized under the guidance of the national defense forces, with the Party's armed forces serving as their reserve. From now on, all those who have reached the age of military service must join the national defense forces. Upon retirement, they will still be listed in the military register of the Party's armed forces in order to complete their military training. The National Socialist Party's guard will also be reorganized in the same spirit. According to the results of the German reorganization of the Party's armed forces, the Party's armed forces must disarm, which has been implemented in most parts of Germany. The only exception is in the areas stipulated for disarmament by the Treaty of Versailles. This is because all civil groups in these areas are similar to the Party's armed forces. According to the provisions of the treaty, their duties are to undertake national defense to a certain extent. (Havas, 25th)

French and German Experts Meet 26

Saar Financial Issues

Recovery of 300 Million Francs

Basel French and German experts are continuing to discuss the financial issues of the Saar region. An agreement has been reached regarding the recovery of French banknotes within the Saar region. These banknotes total approximately 300 million francs. Five percent of this amount will be held by the Bank for International Settlements as collateral for Saar regional bonds, while the remaining ninety-five percent will be used as part of the redemption price for the Saar coal mines and paid into the Bank for International Settlements' account for France. However, the total redemption price was previously agreed upon as 900 million francs, leaving a significant difference. This will be compensated by Germany supplying 1.5 million tons of coal annually for five years. (Havas, 25th)

Hirota Explains Diplomatic Policy in Parliament 27

Proactive Approach to China and Russia

Finance Minister Believes Reform of the Puppet Currency System is Inadvisable

(Tokyo) The House of Representatives convened at 1:20 PM today. First, Mr. Kyōichi Yamamichi, a member of the Kokumin Dōmei (National Alliance), took the floor to raise questions on financial and economic matters, parliamentary politics, and diplomacy, particularly focusing on relations with Manchukuo, as follows:

(1) The currency system of "Manchukuo" is still the same as China, based on silver, which is a great contradiction. Economic cooperation between Japan and Manchukuo cannot take its first step without implementing currency reform. (2) The reform plan for the organs stationed in Manchuria should be based on the government's plan due to the actual situation. However, the handling of the plan is inappropriate, as politics is the sum of the legal system and military force. Interpreting it this way can cause unfortunate events. If law and force without politics are used, it would be the same as going against the ancients.

Finance Minister Takahashi's Answer

The economic relationship between "Manchukuo" and mainland China is inseparable. If China is excluded, there is no way to discuss Manchukuo. Therefore, without considering what will happen to China in the future, one cannot easily talk about currency system reform for "Manchukuo". When it is possible to switch to the gold standard in the future, we can discuss the methods. For now, it is best to maintain the status quo.

Foreign Minister Hirota's Answer

My speech is definitely not a so-called diplomatic document. I truly do not have a single selfish thought on matters related to diplomacy. I will express my personal aims here. Although there may be disagreements, I hope for understanding. I am willing to dedicate my life to diplomacy with China.

Afterwards, Mr. Hitoshi Ashida raised questions about diplomatic policy, which Foreign Minister Hirota answered separately. Finally, regarding international relations, he said, "I will not allow war to break out during my term." Prime Minister Okada also gave answers. The session adjourned at 6:25 PM. (Nippon Dempo News Agency, 25th)

(Tokyo) Foreign Minister Hirota answered Mr. Hitoshi Ashida's questions on the Japan-Russia issue at today's House of Representatives session in the afternoon, stating the following: I plan to propose to the Soviet Union that the Russian, puppet, and Japanese armies withdraw from the borders. My ideal is to have a demilitarized zone like the North China demilitarized zone on the Russian-puppet border. However, if a Japan-Russia non-aggression treaty is not implemented by both sides, it is equivalent to waste paper. Therefore, we will not start work on it first. (Hua Lian News Agency, 25th)

Annihilation of Administrator Incident 31

France Negotiates with Abyssinia

Demanding Security of Border Tranquility

(Paris) The French government, due to the annihilation of a French administrator and over a hundred native soldiers of French Somaliland by Abyssinian tribes, has resolved to seriously negotiate with the Abyssinian government. However, because the Abyssinian Foreign Minister has promised to thoroughly investigate this case, it is necessary to wait for the results of the thorough investigation before deciding on a method. The French government plans to request the Abyssinian government to ensure that the border of French Somaliland will no longer be attacked by Abyssinian tribes. Political circles here are earnestly stating that there are no diplomatic disputes between France and Abyssinia, because the relations between the two countries are very friendly. (Reuters, 25th)

Severe Cold Wave in America 32

Breaks Fifty-Year Record

(New York) The entire country is experiencing a severe cold wave, the worst in fifty years. The number of deaths has reached one hundred, mostly from freezing or drowning. However, a warming trend is expected in a few days. While the northern states and part of the south remain extremely cold, temperatures in the east and southwest have risen. The cold in the Midwest has broken a fifty-year record and is also expected to warm up. New England is currently working to clear the snow. New York City received sixteen inches of snow and is now using over 40,000 people to clear it. While the cold wave is showing signs of waning, there are still major storms in several parts of the country, followed by heavy flooding. Rainfall has broken records. A large part of Washington State has been flooded due to snowmelt and continuous rain. At least fourteen people have drowned in the south. The waters of all rivers have flooded the streets and cities. Many important towns are experiencing traffic congestion due to flooding, and several thousand people are perched on treetops and rooftops and have been rescued by gasoline boats, but there are still many in dangerous places, all calling for help. The situation in Canada is equally dire. Vancouver has been cut off for three days due to heavy snow. Several transcontinental trains have been stopped in the Rocky Mountains due to landslides and avalanches blocking the tracks. Many workers are currently clearing them. (Reuters, 24th)

Simon Defamation Case 33

Defendant Apologizes and Settles the Matter

(London) The Bishop of Dorchester, in a speech at a local Free Church meeting, stated that many members of Parliament and cabinet ministers invest in arms factories, so they are actually the instigators of our wars. He also said that Foreign Secretary Simon overturned the peace movement promoted by the League of Nations due to his investment in arms factories. Simon, believing the words to be defamatory, sued in court. The trial opened today. The plaintiff's lawyer, Mr. Barker, stated that since the lawsuit was filed, the defendant had apologized to Simon and retracted the statement. Simon did not want the defendant to pay damages or litigation costs. The purpose of his lawsuit was to prove the standard of British public life. He added that if anyone makes such unfounded statements in the future, they will be dealt with severely, probably in criminal court rather than civil court. Simon then stated that none of the defendant's words were true. Then, the defendant's lawyer apologized on behalf of his client. Finally, the presiding judge concluded the case, saying that he believed the British Foreign Secretary was lenient to the defendant. Such attacks on British politicians are truly outrageous. (Reuters, 25th)

Page 9

Telegram from Li Rong and Sheng Shicai

Detailing the Current Situation in Xinjiang Province 35

Chiang Kai-shek and Wang Jingwei Send Telegrams of Comfort and Instructions

(Nanjing) Li Rong, Chairman of the Xinjiang Provincial Government, and Sheng Shicai, Border Defense Commissioner, recently telegraphed stating that local newspapers had misunderstood or misrepresented the situation in Xinjiang province and provided clarification on the 15th. Upon receiving this telegram, the central authorities, headed by Chairman Chiang Kai-shek and President Wang Jingwei, sent telegrams of comfort and instructions. Both telegrams are recorded as follows: (Li and Sheng's Telegram) Briefly stated, since the loss of the Northeast, the situation on the border has been precarious. Shicai and others, upon receiving orders from the central government, have worked hard to suppress the rebels and preserve the territory. This can be told to the people of the country without shame. However, recently, various newspapers in the interior have spread rumors about Xinjiang, making unwarranted accusations, fabricating stories, and confusing the public. Shicai and others are distraught and find it difficult to understand. The spread of rumors has little impact on individuals but greatly harms the border situation, causing those who are loyal to the party and the country to feel disappointed. This is regrettable. Furthermore, communication to Xinjiang is difficult, so the truth may not be clear. However, the facts are there and can be verified. Since the April 12th Incident (1927), for three years, all measures have been taken in accordance with the central government's political orders. Shicai, having learned from the past, is constantly vigilant against warlords dividing the land for their own selfish gain. During the departure of Jin Shuren, when the banditry was rampant and imperialists were manipulating the situation, causing ethnic conflicts and mutual killings, the number of disputes and the dangerous environment should be imagined by the people of the country. Shicai and others bear the responsibility of protecting the border and ensuring the safety of the people. We dare not take credit for the work of heaven, but we also bear the responsibility entrusted to us by the territory. However, the rumor-mongers accuse us of colluding with foreigners and engaging in treason. If this is tolerable, what is not tolerable? To make the people of the country understand the truth, we dare to absolutely declare that no country has a single soldier stationed in Xinjiang, no inch of land has been occupied by foreigners, and no organization does not comply with central government orders. As for the so-called treason and communication with foreign countries, we dare to use our personalities as collateral and swear that we have no other intentions. Only after destruction does construction begin. Due to the lack of talent, there is indeed a practice of hiring consultants. However, political orders come from the provincial government, and these personnel can only assist in planning and have no power to command various departments. As for the relationship between Xinjiang and the Soviet Union, it is limited to commerce. Shicai, being aware of the times and knowing the situation, believes that restoring trade with the Soviet Union is beneficial to both breaking the deadlock and developing the economy. It should also be stated that the recently finalized contract between Xinjiang and the Soviet Union for a purely commercial loan is used for various production projects, such as agriculture, industry, commerce, and transportation. In the future, it will be gradually repaid by Xinjiang's local products. The central government is also doing its utmost to carry out the above projects and utilize foreign capital as a foundation, such as the recent cotton and wheat loan. Although the names are different, the uses are the same. Since it does not harm sovereignty and is supported by public opinion, why is there so much doubt and lack of sympathy from the outside world, leading to delays? It is regrettable. In short, Shicai and others know in our hearts that our duty is to gather the ethnic groups and do everything to protect the border and defend the territory, building from destruction and prospering from desolation. All measures are in accordance with central government orders. In order to overcome the current difficulties, we must only adhere to our original intentions to achieve success. However, the rumors in the interior do not occur when the entire Xinjiang is in chaos but when we are striving to govern and working hard. It is enough to hinder local development and create opportunities for the enemy. This is what Shicai and others earnestly hope the people of the country understand. The above is declared to heaven and earth. When Ambassador Yan goes to Russia and passes through Xinjiang, all misunderstandings will not be difficult to clarify at a glance. We dare to ask you to explain to avoid misunderstandings and to convey the truth to the authorities. We look up to Chairman Chiang and President Wang, who take it upon themselves to revive the country and see ten thousand miles ahead. With one word, they will be able to dispel all doubts. Then Xinjiang will be fortunate, and the country will be fortunate. (Chiang and Wang's Telegram) Briefly stated, Chairman Li Rong and Commissioner Sheng Shicai of Dihua (Ürümqi), I have received the telegrams of January 15th forwarded by Governor He Yingqin and the two chairmen and the pacification commissioners of various provinces. The content is sincere and deeply moving. Recalling that Xinjiang has been suffering from continuous turmoil, internal and external troubles, the two of you have held on tenaciously to pacify the local areas. Your efforts are deeply understood by us and are witnessed by the people of the country. Because the roads are distant and communication is cut off, rumors are passed around, leading to inaccuracies. Newspapers must record what they hear, and there may be one or two inaccurate records that are not intentional. We have strictly ordered the responsible authorities to instruct the newspaper offices to publish carefully to avoid confusion. Once traffic is restored and there is frequent communication, the truth will be clear and rumors will stop. The so-called facts speak louder than words. We hope that you both will take a broader view of the situation and not be concerned about trivial matters. This is what we earnestly hope for. Regarding the matters of consultants and loans, the central government takes them extremely seriously. All foreign consultants employed must be through the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and a copy of the employment contract must be submitted to the Executive Yuan for filing. For example, consultants employed by the Military Affairs Commission and the Economic Commission are all handled in accordance with legal procedures. Borrowing foreign loans must be approved by the administrative and central political meetings and reviewed by the Legislative Yuan before they are valid. The cotton and wheat loans from the previous year were all established through this procedure. The central government is still like this. Local governments have no precedents to follow. This is restricted by laws and regulations and is by no means intended to restrict Xinjiang. Xinjiang's position is special, and the situation is very different. It may be necessary to borrow materials from foreign countries. The central government understands this. However, since we know nothing about the facts and details, we cannot provide assistance. For example, regarding the loan, we previously received a telegram from your office to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and the Ministry used the loan contract to review it. Since then, there has been no further mention from your office. Inquiring with the Soviet Russian Embassy here, they are also vague. It is not even certain whether there is a loan, let alone whether it has been approved. You must remember all these events. Now that you have mentioned it, we will also pay attention. Please send the names of the consultants, their nationality, age, position, salary, and term, as well as the full text of the loan contract, to the central government to complete the procedures. In short, the central government and the local government are one entity. Although mountains and rivers may obstruct, our feelings are connected. We hope that you will both work hard to overcome difficulties and jointly support the precarious situation. (Central News Agency, 25th)

Regulations for the Organization of the Xikang Province Establishment Committee

Revised and Approved by the Legislative Yuan

Establish a Committee of up to Seven Members to Execute Administrative Affairs 46

Directly Subordinate to the Executive Yuan and Under the Command of Relevant Ministries

(Nanjing) The Legislative Yuan held its second meeting at 9:00 AM on the 25th. Committee members Guan Suren, Lian Shenghai, Liu Zhendong, and seventy-six others were present. Sun Ke chaired the meeting, and Liang Hancao served as secretary-general. The following matters were reported: (1) Reading of the minutes of the previous meeting. (2) The order from the National Government promulgating the rank table of soldiers of the Army, Navy and Air Force, and ordering it to be implemented. (3) The decision of the Yuan to revise the current budget estimate for the 23rd year of the Guide Huai Committee, which was approved by the National Government, and waiting for instructions to comply. (4) The National Government ordered the promulgation of the general budget of ordinary income and expenditure for the 22nd year of the Weihaiwei Management Office and ordered the Executive and Supervisory Yuan to comply and instructed the Accounting Office to take note. (5) The Shanghai and Peiping Chambers of Commerce submitted the ceremonial notes for common civilities stipulated by the Yuan in order to bring the people into line with proper conduct. Matters for discussion: (1) The Executive Yuan's 439th meeting decided to pass the draft of the Provisional Regulations on Punishment for Hindering the Silver Standard Currency, which was still submitted to the Legislative Yuan for deliberation, and the letter was handled by the National Government to the Yuan. Resolution: Referred to the Finance and Criminal Law Committees for review. (2) Review and amendment of the draft law on Fortified Areas of Fortresses. Resolution: Referred to the Military Affairs Committee for review. (3) The report of the Legislative Yuan's Legal System Committee on the review of the draft Regulations on the Organization of the Xikang Province Establishment Committee. Resolution: Approved as amended according to the review report. As for the amendments to the draft Law on the Organization of County and City Councils and the draft Law on the Election of County and City Councilors, which were temporarily proposed by the Autonomous Law Committee of the Yuan, they will be discussed at the next general meeting. (25th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Regulations for the Organization of the Xikang Province Establishment Committee have been passed. It is expected that preparations will be completed within the next month, and work will begin in early March. The expenses will be subsidized by the central government at around 10,000 yuan per month. The exact amount will be determined after the budget is submitted in the future. (25th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Kuang Chuanyi, a member of the Xikang Province Establishment Committee, took a boat to Hankou on the morning of the 25th and will enter Sichuan to jointly prepare for the establishment of the committee. Leng Rong, a member in Beijing, is also scheduled to set off for Sichuan next week. (25th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) At the regular meeting of the Legislative Yuan on the morning of the 25th, the Regulations on the Organization of the Xikang Province Establishment Committee, consisting of thirteen articles, were passed. Article 1: Before the establishment of the Xikang Provincial Government, a Xikang Province Establishment Committee shall be established to prepare for the establishment of the province and to carry out administrative affairs. Article 2: The committee shall be directly subordinate to the Executive Yuan and subject to the command and supervision of the relevant central ministries. Article 3: The committee may issue orders and formulate separate regulations within the scope of not conflicting with central laws and regulations. However, matters concerning restricting the freedom of the people or increasing the burden on the people shall not be implemented without the approval of the National Government. Article 4: The committee shall consist of five to seven members, appointed by the National Government, and one of the members shall be designated as the chairman. Article 5: The following matters shall be decided by the committee: (1) Matters concerning the province's establishment plan and the development of local economy and culture; (2) Matters concerning the demarcation and change of local administrative regions; (3) Matters concerning the province's budget and final accounts; (4) Matters concerning the local officials' request to the central government for appointment and removal; (5) Matters concerning increasing the burden on the people; (6) Matters concerning the disposal of provincial public property or planning provincial public undertakings; (7) Matters concerning local pacification; (8) Other matters that the Province Establishment Committee deems should be decided. The chairman shall preside over the committee meetings. The resolutions of the committee shall be implemented by the chairman. Article 6: If the chairman is unable to perform his duties due to any reason, one of the members shall be elected to act on his behalf temporarily for a period of two months, and the Executive Yuan shall be notified for record. Article 7: The committee shall have the following divisions: (1) Secretariat: in charge of confidential documents, general affairs, accounting and matters not belonging to other divisions; (2) Department of Civil Affairs: in charge of the appointment and removal of officials, religions, customs and other civil affairs matters in the province; (3) Department of Construction: in charge of industry, transportation, water conservancy and other economic construction matters in the province; (4) Department of Finance: in charge of financial affairs in the province; (5) Department of Education: in charge of education and culture in the province; (6) Department of Security: in charge of police and security matters in the province. If it is necessary to reduce or merge the divisions listed in the preceding paragraph, the committee may submit a request to the Executive Yuan for approval. Article 8: The committee shall have one secretary-general, specially appointed; two secretaries, specially appointed; five secretaries, recommended; and twelve to thirty clerks, appointed. Article 9: The committee may employ specialized technical personnel and employees as needed for its affairs. Article 10: The committee may establish affiliated institutions with the approval of the Executive Yuan as necessary for its affairs. Article 11: The administrative expenses of the committee shall be included in the budget estimate and submitted to the Executive Yuan for verification according to law. Article 12: The rules of procedure for the committee's meetings and the detailed rules for handling affairs in each division shall be determined by the committee and reported to the Executive Yuan for record. Article 13: These regulations shall come into effect on the date of promulgation. (25th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) During the second reading of the draft Regulations on the Organization of the Xikang Province Establishment Committee at the Legislative Yuan on the 25th, Jiao Yitang first reported on the review process, and said that Article 2 of the original draft stated, "The area under the jurisdiction of the Xikang Province Establishment Committee shall be temporarily based on the administrative area of Xikang Province as determined by the Central Resolution in September of the 17th year." The case of the establishment of Xikang Province was proposed to the Central Government by Xue Dubi and others, and approved by the Central Political Council. However, the area under its jurisdiction was not specified in the original resolution. During the review, except for a slight modification of the wording of Article 1, the other parts of the original draft were largely appropriate, so there were not many deletions. Then Wei Tingsheng and others mainly changed the phrase "temporarily based on the administrative area of Xikang Province as determined by the Central Resolution in September of the 17th year" to "temporarily based on the established administrative area of Xikang Province." Di Ying and others believed that whether this article existed or not would not hinder the establishment of Xikang Province, and mainly proposed to delete it. The chairman put the deletion or amendment of this article to a vote, and everyone unanimously agreed to delete the article. There was little controversy over the other articles, and all were omitted and passed in the third reading. (25th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Shanghai commercial organizations, based on the reason that the Japanese trading houses will take the opportunity to rise upon the collection of the transaction tax, appealed to the legislators again. (25th Special Dispatch)

Jiangsu Local Tax Supervision Council Established Yesterday 54

(Zhenjiang) The Jiangsu Provincial Local Tax Supervision Council was established on the afternoon of the 25th. The first meeting was held, and it was decided that the council's address would be the Zhenjiang Chamber of Commerce. In the evening, Zhao hosted a banquet for the members and invited important figures from the province to accompany them. During the banquet, issues such as how to supervise local taxes were discussed. (25th Special Dispatch)
