Guangzhou Market Sluggish 61

Lunar New Year Approaching, Finances Depleted

Treasury Certificates Used Instead of Cash for Settlement of Accounts

Guangzhou Communication: The various stores here are affected by the sluggish market and the collapse of the rural economy. Those who are unable to support themselves have closed down one after another. Even those who can barely maintain the status quo feel that it is difficult to manage the settlement of accounts at the end of the lunar year. The loans released by the silver industry cannot be recovered because most of the stores have closed down. The amount of outstanding loans is about 80%. Therefore, cash is even more scarce. The Chamber of Commerce recently planned to borrow money from the Provincial Bank to seek relief, but credit loans cannot be processed at the Provincial Bank for the time being, and property loans are not being considered because the value of property has fallen sharply in recent years and no one is asking about property. Yesterday, the bank indicated that it was unable to lend money to the merchants. The City Chamber of Commerce had to notify the merchants to use commercial treasury certificates to help with the relief, and to approve the Finance Department to temporarily exempt 20% of the provincial currency for receiving commercial treasury certificates (ie, exempt 20% of the cash, and fully use property mortgage guarantees). The Economic Design Committee of the City Chamber of Commerce reported the case to the public at a meeting yesterday, stating that, according to the letter transferred by the City Chamber of Commerce to the Commercial Treasury Certificate Issuance Committee, the 32nd meeting of the Standing Committee of the Chamber of Commerce decided that, as the Lunar New Year is approaching, for the sake of relieving the market, all settlements, whether using commercial treasury certificates in full or partly, the recipients should accept them. If they refuse to use them, please refer them to the Commercial Mediation Committee of the City Chamber of Commerce for mediation. At the same time, the City Chamber of Commerce yesterday formally notified the various trade associations to inform the stores that all account settlements in the market at the end of the year can use commercial treasury certificates instead of cash, and the recipients must not refuse. If problems arise, they can directly complain to the Commercial Mediation Committee for mediation and interpretation, so as to maintain the market and facilitate the settlement of accounts. (20th)

The Disaster Situation in Various Counties in Western Shandong is Still Severe 62

Floodwater Three or Four Feet Deep, Still Rising

More Than Twenty People Died in Fan County When Ice Floes Hit Boats

Shouzhang Representatives Arrive in Ji'nan to Request Exemption from Head Tax

Ji'nan Communication: The counties of Shouzhang, Shu'a, Yanggu, Fan County, Pu County, etc. in Western Shandong have suffered extremely severe disasters since the Yellow River Changyuan breached its banks in early July of last year, because the area is located between the Jindi and the Yellow River dikes. The floodwater has continued to rise. Up to now, the floodwater is still three or four feet deep in the plains, and has risen another foot recently. During the current ice flood season, the river channel is not flowing smoothly, and there is more overflow. Ice blocks are piled up like mountains. In Caojiazhuang, Dongguan, Fan County, a ferry boat was broken by ice floes the other day. Twenty-seven passengers fell into the water and were tragically drowned. Only three or four people were rescued, and the rest died. It is said to be tragic. In the autumn of last year, the disaster-stricken counties submitted reports to the provincial government, reporting the disaster situation and requesting exemption from head tax. The provincial government exempted Yanggu, Fan County, and Dong'a counties. However, Shouzhang was only allowed to be exempted by one-tenth. In fact, the disaster situation in Shouzhang is also extremely severe. The disaster area is more than 150 li long from east to west and 10 to 30 li wide from north to south. The Ji'nan Red Swastika Society sent personnel to Shouzhang in October of last year to allocate 5,000 yuan in disaster relief. Zhao Mingyuan, the commander of the First Route Militia, recently arrived in Shouzhang and saw that the disaster situation was extremely serious. He gave 4,000 yuan as relocation expenses for the people. More than 2,000 people have now registered. The severity of the tragedy can be imagined. However, the former county magistrate Wu Shouqi's report on the disaster situation was not detailed enough, so the provincial government only approved the exemption of one-tenth of the head tax. The current county magistrate Zhou Ziqin is urging the collection of the head tax very urgently, and the people are really unable to pay. Moreover, the current disaster situation is more serious than before. The disaster victims have no place to live and no food or clothing. The spring planting season is approaching, but the Yellow River water has not receded, and the farmers will have no hope in the future. Therefore, they specially elected ten representatives Wang Yufeng, Zhang Tongheng, Yang Xinzhi, Nie Huadong, Meng Guangrong, Hou Xifeng, Jiang Zungan, Sun Ruyin, Meng Zhaoshan, and Wu Yongxiang to Ji'nan to petition the Department of Civil Affairs, the Department of Finance, and the provincial government to approve the exemption of the head tax and request that the dike be closed as soon as possible to save the people in the disaster. (24th)

Songjiang Fengjing Wei Family Robbery Case Results in Two Deaths 63

In Fengjing Chaowu Township, Lüzi Village, at the home of farmer Wei Guihe, on the night of the 22nd around 11 PM, more than ten bandits arrived, using bamboo poles and wooden ladders to climb over the wall and enter. The bandits spoke with local accents and Wenzhou accents, wielding handguns and flashlights, forcing the family to reveal the location of their hidden money. The homeowner, Wei Guihe, was startled awake from his sleep and hurriedly tried to escape onto the roof, intending to avoid them elsewhere. Unfortunately, he carelessly fell, injuring his left leg. The homeowner's wife, Zhu, heard the commotion and went outside to call for help, mistakenly arriving at Nan Ye by the Jing Port. The bandits pursued her relentlessly, and in the darkness, she fell into the river and drowned. The homeowner's losses amounted to approximately 44 yuan in paper money, 32 jiao in coins, three leather jackets, over twenty silk garments, six bolts of cloth, and one suitcase. It is said that the gang of bandits came from the Xujia Yan Bridge. The family has already reported the incident to the police station for investigation.

Jiading Offers Reward for Apprehending Wire-Cutting Criminals 64

The Jinghu long-distance telephone lines have been repeatedly stolen and cut in Jurong and this county recently. The number of incidents has been quite large. The county government has been ordered by the province to conduct investigations and provide effective protection. County Magistrate Xu has offered a reward for the apprehension of the criminals who stole the telephone wires. A reward of one hundred yuan will be given for the capture of the criminals and the stolen goods. A reward of five hundred yuan will be given for providing information leading to their capture.

Suzhou Suzhou City Prison Status 65

Chen Fumin, a special consultant from the Ministry of Justice, came to Suzhou to inspect the prisons in Suzhou City and completed his report yesterday (the 25th). The main points are as follows: (1) Jiangsu Third Prison in Xiaoliu Zhen Alley has 80 communal prison cells and 12 sick wards, with a capacity of 500 inmates. Currently, it holds 1,030 inmates, with monthly expenses of 5,200 yuan. (2) The Third Sub-prison in Siqian Street and the High Court Detention Center have 113 communal prison cells, 8 separate rooms, 15 women's cells, and 10 sick rooms, originally intended to hold 500 inmates. Currently, it holds 191 convicted prisoners and 1,014 detainees, with monthly expenses of over 6,200 yuan. Each of these two prisons has five workshops. (3) The High Court Detention Sub-center on Guwu Road has eight large rooms and houses 280 inmates. (4) The temporary holding center for convicted prisoners at Shizi Kou has 44 prison cells, with a capacity of 430 inmates. Currently, it holds 492 inmates, with monthly expenses of over 2,600 yuan. (5) The Wu County Local Court Detention Center has 22 prison cells and currently houses 7 inmates awaiting third trial, 22 awaiting execution, 68 awaiting first or second trial, and 59 who have not been prosecuted, with monthly expenses of 1,250 yuan. The report also includes suggestions for improvement, divided into several categories, including disciplining, reforming sanitation facilities, improving work programs, relieving inmate congestion, and providing temporary construction funds, with detailed recommendations.

Changshu 66

Dispatching Troops to Protect Steamboat Passengers

As the end of the lunar year approaches, the county government believes that security is especially important during the customary year-end accounting period for businesses. Furthermore, this county is suffering from drought, and starving people are everywhere. Currently, in addition to working with the drought relief association to actively raise funds for spring relief, special attention is being paid to petty thieves and bandits during the winter defense period. Military forces have been assigned to various key towns for prevention. Now, steamboat managers have been summoned to the county government for discussions. Starting today, for a period of half a month, four security team soldiers will be assigned to each steamboat to provide protection along the way. The soldiers' food and lodging will be provided by the steamboat, and they are not allowed to make any other demands, in order to ensure the safety of travelers. The county has also sent letters to neighboring counties such as Wuxi, Suzhou, Kunshan, and Cheng, urging them to implement similar measures simultaneously.

Special Article

Enemy? Friend? 67

Xu Daolin

丨Examination of Sino-Japanese Relations丨

1. Introduction 丨 The Stalemate Between China and Japan

There are already many papers discussing the Sino-Japanese problem. There are also many opinions expressed by politicians and scholars from both China and Japan, whether they are specialized or general. But I dare to say that very few people from both public and private sectors in both countries can truly consider the ultimate interests of the country regarding the Sino-Japanese problem, without being driven by emotions or politeness, or blinded by temporary errors. We can at least say that the positive understanding of the problem is really not enough. Many tragedies in the international community are caused by a temporary difference, which leads to irreparable disasters. In order to break the stalemate between China and Japan, to prevent it from becoming more and more hopeless, and to establish peace in East Asia and eliminate the chances of war, it is necessary to conduct an honest review of the Sino-Japanese problem, without avoiding or concealing anything, and to make an honest criticism.

I am not an expert in international politics. This article is based entirely on common sense and facts, and it is a purely objective statement of truth and reason for reflection by both China and Japan. I don't need to repeat what has already been discussed by general politicians, but this article will try to state as much as possible and without concealing anything that is generally ignored or avoided, whether I am guilty or not, let the readers decide.

First of all, I dare to say that most intelligent Chinese people know that the Japanese will not ultimately be our enemies, and that China must ultimately have the necessity of working hand in hand with Japan. This is the conclusion based on a thorough consideration of the general trend of the world and the past, present and future of China and Japan (if they do not perish together). I think there should be quite a few Japanese people who hold the same view. But so far, not only has the stalemate not been broken, and there is no sign of renewing relations between the two countries, but also no glimmer of dawn can be found, just delaying the problem and letting nature take its course. Mankind has progressed to the twentieth century, but it still cannot directly recognize the facts, but is covering up and lacking courage and sincerity, which is really confusing.

2. Explain the Advantages and Disadvantages of Prolonging the Stalemate from China's Standpoint

From China's perspective, the Chinese Nationalist Party is currently dominating Chinese politics. There is no doubt that the Nationalist Party should believe in Mr. Sun Yat-sen's teachings. Mr. Sun Yat-sen once said, "If there were no Japan in East Asia, China would have been divided or jointly managed long ago." He also said, "From the day Japan mobilizes to the day it opens to attack China, it will take at most ten days. If China breaks off relations with Japan, Japan can destroy China within ten days." (Fifth Lecture on Nationalism) There are many other words in various speeches and documents that prove that China and Japan are interdependent and mutually beneficial if they cooperate, and both will lose if they are enemies. Originally, from the perspective of the general trend of the world, if China thinks from the long-term future, China and Japan should cooperate with each other and there is no reason to be enemies to the end. Although there are now many citizens who are motivated by the current hatred and are quite willing to perish with Japan, the authorities of the Chinese Nationalist Party, since they have assumed the heavy responsibility of national security, should think from the big picture and have a dignified plan to be loyal to the interests of the country. We certainly know that the initiative in the Sino-Japanese problem is entirely in Japan's hands. When Japan has no intention of easing the situation, China cannot ease it alone. However, the current policy of "resisting while negotiating" is really only enough to show the helplessness of the authorities. Now there is another kind of people who imagine what China will do when Russia, Japan, or the United States goes to war, or even when World War II breaks out, and therefore advocate that China should absolutely not participate in the war and should strictly maintain neutrality. However, everyone knows that once the war starts, China will never be able to maintain neutrality to the end. The most likely position will probably be not actively standing on one side, but opposing the other side, or it can be said that when one side forces us or destroys our neutrality, we will resist him at the expense of sacrifice. But this is still no different from joining the war, and this cannot maintain neutrality and is in a passive position of being forced to participate, which is of no benefit to China, and will inevitably fall into the most miserable situation. So I say that it is better to say that we should strictly maintain neutrality than to say that we are prepared to sacrifice and participate in the war. If we want to say that we are standing on one side to participate in the war, it is better to say that we are resisting the other side. Therefore, it can be seen that it is no different from a fool's dream for China to maintain neutrality in World War II or to hope to gain some benefits by taking advantage of the situation. I believe that the only way for China at present is to try its best to eliminate the chances of war. And if we want to eliminate the chances of war, we must at least find a solution to the Sino-Japanese problem, which is one of the reasons for causing the war. If the Sino-Japanese problem is solved, the world situation will change, and the war between Russia, the United States, and Japan may not happen. Even if there is still a war between Russia, Japan, or the United States, China can have a clear position, deal with it freely, and not be constrained in the slightest. Therefore, whether from the perspective of Mr. Sun Yat-sen's teachings and the permanent interests of the country, or from the perspective of responding to the current international situation, China should by no means allow the Sino-Japanese stalemate to continue indefinitely without seeking a solution.

3. Considering for Japan, Explain the Advantages and Disadvantages of Prolonging the Stalemate

From Japan's perspective, from the September 18th Incident to the present, from Uchida to Hirota, from the occupation of the four northeastern provinces, the subsequent withdrawal from the League of Nations, to the tough statement on April 17 last year, and to the present, although there have been repeated verbal slogans of "promoting and maintaining peace in East Asia," what they have done has been to increase the crisis of peace in East Asia, and they have been actively pursuing their tough policy towards China, and there is no sign of change. We certainly know that since Japan threw such an amazing bomb at China and the world three years ago, it is now going straight forward under some kind of ideal, whether it wants to or not. The country's politicians and military departments have their own plans for the world and China, or their own plans are very detailed. However, as outsiders, we can at least say that Japan's plans are not foolproof in terms of its strategy towards China. When discussing Japan's relations with China, we must also discuss its intricate relations with Russia, the United States (and Britain). On the one hand, because Japan wants to carry out its continental policy and the ideal of dominating the Pacific, defeating its powerful enemies, and unifying East Asia, it has aroused the jealousy of Russia and the United States. On the other hand, what the Japanese authorities use to deceive their people is that if they do not acquire Manchuria and Mongolia, they will not be able to eliminate the threat to Japan's national defense. In other words, Japan must manage Manchuria and Mongolia in order to prepare for war against Russia and the United States. We are now also taking a purely objective attitude to consider for Japan. Internationally, whether in terms of strategy or political strategy, in addition to the front, we should of course also consider the side and the back. If there are enemies on the side and back, and if the military strength of these enemies is used properly, it can be more effective than two, three, or even ten times the strength on the front. This is well known to any political strategist or strategist in the world. Now, if Japan wants to start a war with the United States to the east, China is on its back. If it wants to start a war with the Soviet Union to the north, China is on its side. Therefore, if Japan wants to prepare for war against the United States and Russia, if it does not eliminate the concerns on the side and back, it will not only have no chance of winning, but it will not even be possible to start a war. However, there are two ways to eliminate the concerns on the side and back. One way is to absolutely control this neighboring country with force so that it cannot cause trouble. The other way is to form a harmonious relationship with this neighboring country on the side and back. Now that the Japanese are not cooperating with China from the harmonious aspect, Japan's plan is obviously to take the method of controlling China by force. However, can Japan absolutely achieve the goal of controlling China? Moreover, in our opinion, since the relations between China and Japan have deteriorated to this point, it is not enough to just control China, but it must completely destroy China before it starts a war against the United States or Russia. If Japan cannot destroy China within ten days as Mr. Sun Yat-sen said, Japan's position is very dangerous. Because if Japan takes three months or half a year to destroy China, the United States or Russia will definitely not sit idly by and wait for Japan to deal with China calmly, and will force Japan to fight a quick battle. However, based on our observation of the facts, Japan has occupied the Northeast for three years. Not only can the Northeast Volunteer Army not be eliminated, but how can the civilian guns in Shenyang County be collected as scheduled? Based on this fact, can Japan after all completely control China or even destroy China in the shortest period of time, such as within ten days? As for why Mr. Sun Yat-sen clearly stated that Japan can destroy China within ten days, it should be known that Mr. Sun Yat-sen's words were to see through Japan's ambition and possibility to occupy important places in China within ten days, so he especially emphasized his words to warn the Chinese people. He also knew very well that Japan can only occupy important transportation areas in China within ten days, but cannot destroy China's 4.5 million square miles of land and 480 million people? Now that we understand this meaning, we can observe from various facts and situations whether Japan has the possibility of completely controlling China or destroying China?

(1) In terms of controlling China, Japan must of course first use its naval power to blockade China's coast. However, China is still in a semi-colonial status, and European and American countries have intricate political and economic relations with China, especially Britain's relations are even closer, which is not just related to the interests of one or two countries. If Japan wants to do this, it will not only be an enemy of China, but also an enemy of Russia and the United States, and will force Britain and the whole world to be enemies. Originally, controlling the coast of China was for the convenience of fighting against Russia or the United States, but before the main battle has begun, it has expanded the scope of hostility to the whole world. Is this a beneficial strategy? This is in terms of the sea.

(2) On the land side, what we can believe that Japan is actively planning is to create the second and third "Manchukuo," that is, what is generally said to expand the scope of aggression to create the so-called "North China Country" or "Mongolia Country." But is this allowed by Japan's power? First of all, in terms of economy, how much military expenditure has Japan spent since it sent troops to Manchuria to create the "puppet state"? This is well known to the world, and the continuous increase in the amount of fiscal deficit in the country is also well known to the world. Now, if it expands the scope of aggression, it must be known that managing North China will definitely not be as easy as seizing the three northeastern provinces. First, the incident happened unprepared, and second, the people's morale and strength in North China and the level of people's knowledge are also different from those in the three northeastern provinces who have been under Japanese influence for a long time. If Japan really wants to create the second and third puppet organizations in North China or Mongolia that it imagines, the military strength consumed and the expenses incurred will definitely be doubled compared with the past. And in areas such as Inner Mongolia, the wilderness is barren, with little production and no income at all. If it insists on managing it, it will cost twice as much. This is in terms of its direct economic impact. In terms of indirect impact, if Japan must further expand the scope of aggression, the Chinese people's boycott movement will not be suppressed by any force. At that time, whether Japan still has commercial or other industries that can stand in China is not difficult to imagine. Furthermore, in terms of military affairs and the required military strength, first take "Manchukuo" as an example. The Japanese troops stationed in "Manchukuo" are said to be five divisions on the surface, but in fact we know that there are more than 100,000 people. With more than 100,000 troops, they still cannot ensure the so-called "Manchukuo" The security within the territory is constantly threatened by the Volunteer Army. Then, if Japan wants to create the same second and third pseudo-organizations as "Manchukuo," it must send at least 200,000 troops to deal with it. The total number of Japanese regular troops is only 17 divisions. Even if all of them are transferred, it will not be enough. The maintenance and suppression of security in the country and Korea also require considerable military strength. At this point, it will inevitably conscript reserve and reserve soldiers. In this way, Japan will be formally at war with China; and being formally at war with China is not what I said above, just controlling the area in northern China. In this way, it will take the supporting battlefield as the main battlefield, and it will completely abandon its main enemy. If Japan takes this wrong step, it will be doomed to its own demise. China will not be afraid of this kind of meaningful sacrifice, and will rather be happy to accept it without hesitation.

(3) If Japan officially uses troops against China for any reason, China's military strength is not as good as Japan's, and it will inevitably suffer great sacrifices. This is something that Chinese people cannot deny. However, Japan's difficulty lies in this. It is precisely because China has no strength that it is its strength that cannot be easily insulted. When a war begins, in countries with equal strength, the final battle is the end of the war. However, in countries with absolutely unequal military strength, such as Japan fighting against China, there is no such thing as a formal final battle. It will not be the end of the war until Japan can occupy every square mile of China's land and completely destroy China. When the two countries start a war, it is essential to occupy the political center. However, when fighting against China, if the capital is occupied by force, it will not be able to control China's fate. (Because China is still in the period of unfinished revolution, which will be discussed in detail below) At most, Japan can only occupy some cities with convenient transportation and important seaports in China, but it can never occupy all of China's 4.5 million square miles. When all the important cities and seaports in China are occupied, China will indeed fall into extreme distress and sacrifice. However, how can Japan completely eliminate China's existence? Even if the four northeastern provinces are occupied as an example, China's loss of this important territory is of course an extremely serious loss. However, from the perspective of the nature of the National Government in the revolutionary period, temporary gains and losses are almost irrelevant, and it is rather a blessing in disguise. Because we have heard the authorities of the Chinese Nationalist Party say: "The revolutionary party should of course be responsible for recovering the Northeast, but the revolutionary party is not responsible for losing the Northeast." The author is not a member of the Nationalist Party, and I do not want to say whether this statement is a self-justification of the Nationalist Party. In fact, before the September 18th Incident, the Northeast was only nominally under the National Government, and the military, political, and financial powers were completely independent. At least it can be said that it was not within the scope of the revolutionary forces. However, in the past, it was only nominal, but now it has even lost its name. However, although it seems to have fallen, in fact, since the Northeast was occupied, the Northeast Army has been completely unified under the central government, and the people of the Northeast have thoroughly recognized the meaning of nationalism, and spiritually are more closely under the unified China. Based on this evidence, it can be known that if Japan continues to invade and reduce China's territory as a good plan, the result will only be to make China follow the example of Turkey when it abandoned Europe and retreated to Asia, shorten the front line, and try its best to fight for survival. At that time, the lives of the people of the two countries will be sacrificed, and the tragedy cannot be predicted. However, can Japan ultimately achieve the goal of completely destroying China after the war?

Based on the above points. It can be seen that whether Japan is preparing for war against Russia and the United States, or carrying out its traditional continental policy of 50 years ago, and using military force to oppress or invade China, from Japan's standpoint, it is definitely an attempt with great sacrifice and no guarantee. In other words, whether it is controlling China or destroying China, it is impossible. As for the international community's condemnation and Japan's internal crisis, I don't need to say more in this article. There are also many people of insight in Japan who are very worried about Japan's future. However, in my opinion, Japan really has no reason to go its own way to the end. If it puts aside its prejudices and recognizes the facts, and wants to change its course, then it will be back on the right path.

The formation of great mistakes in the international community has both primary and secondary causes. Often, it is not only one party that has made mistakes, but both parties must have their own mistakes. Looking back at the period from before and after the September 18th Incident to the present, whether it is the Chinese side or the Japanese side, they all have their own errors in their understanding of the general situation and of each other, as well as in their measures. Some of these errors have become past, and some continue to follow the wrong path and constantly create new errors. Since this article wants to honestly review Sino-Japanese relations, it should of course point out all the errors on both sides, and then it can determine the path to be taken to solve the problem. (To be continued)

World Press Congress 74

Seeking Chinese Members

Huang Xianzhao Appointed as Chinese Vice-President

According to the Central News Agency, the World Press Congress was founded in 1915 by American press leaders and has continued for nearly twenty years. It has convened journalists from various countries in San Francisco, Honolulu, Geneva, and Mexico City, achieving significant results. The next congress was originally scheduled to be held in Melbourne, Australia, in March of this year. However, the organizers are now aiming to expand the congress and plan to first hold a large-scale membership drive to strengthen its foundation before convening the congress. In China, the congress has invited Mr. Huang Xianzhao to serve as the Chinese Vice-President, responsible for recruiting Chinese members. Mr. Huang, believing that the Chinese press may not be fully aware of the congress's history and mission, has provided a summary of the congress's history and regulations for reference.

History of the Congress 75

Under the leadership of its president, Mr. Bell, the World Press Congress is currently undergoing reorganization and expansion in terms of membership and work. The next congress, originally scheduled for the latter part of March this year, has been postponed to allow ample time and opportunity for the congress to develop. The congress is now adding vice-presidents, who are being nominated based on the national and political boundaries of various countries around the world. There are currently seventy-five vice-presidents, all of whom are enthusiastic supporters and dedicated collaborators, and are working hard to recruit members for this grand endeavor. The congress offers three types of membership: individual membership, for anyone working in the press, regardless of nationality or job title, with annual dues of US$5; corporate membership, for newspapers, magazines, and specialized publications issued by businesses, with annual dues of US$50; and basic membership, for major news agencies, daily newspapers, and news distribution organizations around the world, with annual dues of US$100 or an amount approved by the Executive Committee. All members are entitled to all the benefits of the congress, such as attending meetings, discussing congress affairs, participating in voting, and receiving congress publications. The World Press Congress was founded in 1915 and has held meetings in San Francisco, Honolulu, Geneva, and Mexico City. Representatives from twenty to thirty countries have participated in the meetings, engaging in frank discussions on various issues related to the press. All resolutions and meeting records are printed and distributed to the members. Overall, the achievements of the congress can be summarized as: (1) promoting communication among press workers from various countries and jointly discussing various issues; (2) facilitating the reduction of news cable rates; (3) assisting journalists imprisoned in countries where freedom of speech is restricted, to ensure fair trials; (4) promoting journalism education; (5) supporting the circulation of international news; (6) supporting the exchange of newspaper reporters, journalists, and professors and students of journalism schools in various countries; (7) planning a journalist accreditation system, and so on. In addition, there are various new plans being considered, such as requesting governments to recognize foreign correspondents, appointing press attachés to embassies and consulates, improving newspaper standards, investigating press issues, and advocating for freedom of speech. The congress will also publish regular reports and maintain close contact with vice-presidents in various countries. The current address of the congress is Jay of Neff Hall, Missouri, USA. The sole purpose of the congress is, as Honorary President Dr. William has stated, to enhance the well-being and service of journalists and the press around the world. Therefore, all the officers of the congress welcome assistance, criticism, and suggestions from all parties.

Articles of Association 76

The articles of association of the Congress are listed as follows: Article 1: The name of this association is the World Press Congress. Article 2: The purpose of this association is to promote the mission of the press through all honest means, using meetings, discussions, and cooperation. The Congress meetings may discuss various issues directly related to the press, but may not discuss religion, politics, or government policies. Article 3: Any person from any country engaged in the press, whose work promotes the highest standards and greatest benefits of the press, may become a member of this association. Article 4: The officers of this association, elected at each meeting, are as follows: one honorary president, one president, vice-presidents, two representatives from each country, one secretary and treasurer, and nine members of the executive committee, including the honorary president, the president, the secretary and treasurer, and six other members. The Executive Committee shall establish a council, chaired by the Honorary President, with no more than fifty members. Its task is to provide advice and assistance to the Congress and its committees on policies, organization, and activities. Vacancies on the committee shall be filled by the Executive Committee. Article 5: The time and place of the Congress meetings shall be determined by the Executive Committee. Article 6: These articles of association may be amended by the Executive Committee and submitted to any Congress for decision.

Representatives Requesting Tax Reduction 77

Gu Xin Yi and Others Return to Shanghai

Reportedly the Exchange Tax Will Be Postponed for One Year

Tax Rate to Be Based on Ad Valorem, Securities Tax Determined to Be Completely Exempted

Stamp Tax One in Ten Thousand, Yarn, Flour, and Grains One in Ten Thousand

According to the Da Gong She, Gu Xin Yi, Shao Wenmei, Zhan Liansheng, Wang Jiafu, and other representatives from the five exchanges in this city who attended the Legislative Yuan's review meeting in Beijing, returned to Shanghai yesterday morning on the Beijing-Shanghai express train. The Da Gong She reporter interviewed Mr. Gu Xin Yi, chairman of the Grains Exchange, yesterday to inquire about the review meeting. He provided the following details:

Satisfactory Results from Vigorous Advocacy at the Meeting 78

I (Gu referring to himself), along with all the representatives from the five exchanges, traveled to Beijing on the 23rd of this month and arrived in Beijing early the next morning. After resting at the hotel, we immediately went to the Legislative Yuan to attend the meeting. The agenda of the Economic and Financial Committees' review meeting stipulated that the representatives of the Ministry of Finance would report on their tax collection proposals in the morning, with Mr. Xu Kan, Director of the Currency Department of the Ministry of Finance, presenting the report in three points (the content was reported in yesterday's newspaper). The formal review meeting was held in the afternoon, allowing representatives from each exchange to attend. Fifty to sixty legislators participated in the review that day. Each exchange vigorously argued against the imposition of a transaction tax, given the business conditions and the depressed state of industry and commerce. The atmosphere at the meeting was very tense. The representatives from the exchanges, bearing the overall mission, seized this final opportunity to gather various facts and make the strongest possible arguments. Fortunately, the two committees of the Legislative Yuan were sympathetic to the difficulties of businesses, and the results were quite satisfactory.

Tax Rate Based on Ad Valorem, Postponed for One Year 79

The transaction tax, as stipulated by the Ministry of Finance, was divided into two types: "ad valorem" and "specific duty." It was also planned that after being reviewed and passed by the Legislative Yuan, it would be implemented starting from February 1. As a result of the vigorous advocacy of the representatives from the five exchanges, the original plan to use "specific duty" as the standard for cotton, cotton yarn, flour, grains, wheat, soybeans, red sorghum, bean cake, bean oil, and other items was uniformly changed to "ad valorem" for calculating taxes. As for the official start date of tax collection, the representative of the Ministry of Finance acknowledged a one-year postponement. However, the representatives of the exchanges believed that the social and economic situation in recent years has been depressed and industry and commerce have been declining. It is difficult to predict whether industry and commerce will turn around and prosper after one year. They still advocated for an indefinite postponement, and that the tax should only be levied if the business of the exchanges truly improves. This is now being decided by five legislators. However, the one-year postponement has already been agreed to by the Ministry of Finance and should not be a problem.

Securities Exempted from All Taxes, Reduced Burden 80

Regarding the taxes on the five exchanges for gold, securities, cotton cloth, flour, and grains, the tax rates proposed by the Ministry of Finance were: 0.0125% for securities, approximately 0.01% for stamp tax per transaction, approximately 0.025% for cotton cloth, and approximately 0.06-0.07% for flour and grains. During the review meeting of the Legislative Yuan, it was argued that the securities with value (i.e., public bonds) are all issued by the central and local governments, and taxing them in the same way would adversely affect the future of the public bond market. Most legislators advocated for exemption. The review also led to a reduction in the stamp tax rate from 0.01% to 0.001%, and a reduction in the tax rate for cotton cloth from 0.025% and for flour and grains from 0.06-0.07% to 0.01%. The principles have been initially determined and are unlikely to change.

Five Legislators Appointed to Conduct Investigation 81

In order to understand the business conditions of each exchange and as a basis for the review, the Economic and Financial Committees of the Legislative Yuan appointed five legislators, Chen Changheng, Chen Jianru, Zheng Hongnian, Zhang Zhihan, and Liu Zhendong, to conduct an investigation. The initial review was originally scheduled for this morning (i.e., yesterday morning). All representatives of the exchanges were prepared to stay in Beijing to make further statements. Subsequently, the Legislative Yuan notified that due to procedural issues, it was postponed to tomorrow (i.e., today). We (Gu referring to himself), due to the Chinese New Year and the complexity of various affairs, have returned to Shanghai first. Mu Ouchu, Zhang Weiru, Xu Busun, and the representatives of the brokers' associations of each exchange will likely return to Shanghai after attending the initial review meeting of the five legislators.

Second Review to Be Held Next Month 82

The second review meeting of the Economic and Financial Committees of the Legislative Yuan has been decided to be held in two weeks. It is not yet confirmed whether the appointed five legislators will come to Shanghai to conduct an on-site investigation of each exchange. The Exchange Federation will convene a joint meeting with the brokers' associations after the representatives return to Shanghai to collect information on the business conditions and financial status of the past three years and submit it to the Legislative Yuan for reference.

Zhejiang Province's Two Million Loan 83

Banks Made Payments Yesterday

Funds Have Been Fully Transferred to the Finance Department by Bank of China

Pledged Public Bonds Given to Respective Borrowing Banks for Safekeeping

According to Xin Xin She, the Zhejiang Provincial Government used local public bonds of 3.34 million, discounted to borrow 2 million from Bank of China and other Shanghai banks as collateral. The loan contract, after being approved by the Zhejiang Provincial Government's meeting, was sent to Shanghai on the 23rd and distributed by Bank of China, the representative of the syndicate, to each borrowing bank for signing. The respective borrowing banks had transferred the amount they subscribed to Bank of China at one time starting at 9:00 AM yesterday to be transferred to the Zhejiang Finance Department for receipt. Details of each situation are noted as follows:

Funds Transferred Yesterday 84

Starting at 9:00 AM yesterday, each borrowing bank transferred the amount they subscribed to Bank of China at one time. The bank then transferred the funds to its Hangzhou branch to be directly transferred to the Finance Department for receipt. The amounts are as follows: Bank of China 610,000, Bank of Communications 320,000, Zhejiang Industrial Bank 186,000, Zhejiang Industrial Corporation 160,000, Bank of Shanghai 120,000, China Industrial Bank, Sze Ming Bank, China General Chamber of Commerce Bank, Continental Bank, and Jin Cheng Bank 80,000 each, Ken Yip Bank and Chung Nam Bank 70,000 each, and Salt Bank 64,000, totaling 2 million. When the Zhejiang Finance Department received the funds, it handed over Zhejiang local public bonds with a face value of 3.34 million from 1934 to the syndicate representatives for distribution to each borrowing bank for safekeeping.

Change of Use 85

The Zhejiang Finance Department originally intended to use public bonds with a face value of 10 million as collateral for 6 million for use. However, with the Chinese New Year approaching, the banks only agreed to lend 2 million first. Therefore, the original intended use of 6 million and the allocation of funds has now been changed as follows: (1) 1 million for construction expenses; (2) 500,000 for government expenses; (3) the remaining 500,000 will be used to pay off various miscellaneous debts.

Chen Qinshi and Others Launch Artificial Silk Factory 86

Shanghai Financial Circles Agree to Invest

Factory Site Decided to Be in Hangzhou

According to the Guomin She, Zhejiang gentry Chen Qinshi and Xu Jisheng, in view of the large-scale dumping of artificial silk in China, which has led to a sharp decline in the Chinese silk business, which is on the verge of collapse, have joined with gentry and merchants in Hangzhou and Huzhou to launch a large-scale artificial silk factory. Financial circles in Shanghai have also agreed to invest. A meeting was held to discuss implementation methods. It was decided that the factory site would be in Hangzhou, and it would also employ unemployed silk factory workers. Another meeting will be held soon to discuss all the specific methods.

Private Postal Bureaus Have Virtually Ceased Operations 87

Reorganization Into Transport Bureaus Considered Impossible by Peers

The Municipal Government Is Discussing Relief Measures for Employees

According to the Da Gong She, the peak seasons for private postal bureaus to receive private letters are during the Chinese Dragon Boat Festival, Mid-Autumn Festival, and Chinese New Year. Each bureau would work extra shifts to deliver them. During each New Year, factories, shops, or individuals sending silver dollar packages, letters, and so on are even more crowded than usual. Since the Ministry of Communications ordered them to cease operations last year and began intercepting letters in January of this year, private postal bureaus have disappeared. The allowed sending of silver dollar packages, etc., is also impossible to receive due to the inconvenience of carrying letters. With the Chinese New Year approaching, business has completely stopped. More than sixty private postal bureaus in the northern and southern districts and the concessions of this city have virtually declared their closure.

Difficulty in Reorganization: After the Ministry of Communications' order not to extend the closure deadline reached Shanghai, some letter merchants in this city, in order to find a way to maintain their livelihoods, planned to reorganize into transport bureaus, specializing in remittances of silver dollar packages, cargo, and so on. The principle was decided by the general representative, Yin Yuantong, and others in a meeting, and letters were sent to peers in various places to solicit opinions. According to the replies from most letter merchants, they believe it is practically difficult. The reasons are: (1) all remittances or entrusted packages and cargo must be accompanied by letters. Now that private letters are not allowed to be delivered, reorganization into transport bureaus is also futile, and senders are unwilling to take this extra step; (2) the business scope and nature of transport bureaus are completely different from those of private postal bureaus, and their financial strength must be sufficient to proceed. Moreover, sending silver dollar packages, etc., without accompanying letters is prone to malpractice and involves great risk.

Municipal Government Relief: The national private postal bureaus previously requested the central government to withdraw its order to ban private postal bureaus. The General Assembly of General Representatives was fully authorized to handle this. Now that the Ministry of Communications has replied that it cannot be salvaged, and reorganization into transport bureaus is difficult, most representatives have dispersed and left Shanghai. Regarding the relief of more than a thousand employees in this city, the municipal government has previously ordered the Social Affairs and Public Security Bureaus to conduct a thorough investigation and propose relief measures for the government to review. It is now heard that the points agreed upon by the two bureaus regarding employee relief have been submitted to the municipal government for proper handling.

Ministry of Communications Constructs Shanghai-Guangdong Wireless Telephone Project 92

Materials Arrived in Shanghai, Construction Has Begun

Expected to Be in Operation Before Double Ten Day This Year

According to the Da Gong She, in order to facilitate communication between Shanghai and Guangdong, the Ministry of Communications has decided to build a wireless telephone system between Shanghai and Guangdong. It has commissioned the China Electric Company to purchase a large number of wireless telephone materials from the United Kingdom, which have all arrived in Shanghai, totaling more than 100 pieces. They are currently stored at the Zhenru International Radio Station.

Construction Has Begun: The Ministry of Communications has chosen Zhenru because of its vast land and convenient transportation. Therefore, the Shanghai station for the Shanghai-Guangdong wireless telephone has been surveyed and decided to be built there. Construction has begun in recent days. In Guangzhou, the local communications authorities have also ordered construction. Meanwhile, Mr. Sparg, manager of the China Electric Company, has been commissioned by the Ministry of Communications to inspect the progress of the project in Guangdong.

Operation in October: The total construction cost of the entire project, with all the machines and components being high-quality materials from abroad, is estimated to be 700,000 yuan, one of the largest electrical projects in China in recent years. It is expected to be in operation before Double Ten Day this year. However, if the project is subject to unexpected obstacles, it may be delayed until next spring before it can be officially put into operation.

Famine Relief Association 93

Held Sixth Meeting Yesterday

Formed Seed Preparation and Distribution Research Committee

More Than 100,000 Yuan Raised in City-Wide Donations

The All-Provinces Famine Relief Association held its sixth meeting yesterday at 4:00 PM at the Renji Hall on Yunnan Road. More than twenty people attended, including Xu Shiying.

Chairman Xu Shiying Reported: 1. The Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau sent a letter requesting assistance for 165 Hunan famine refugees, including Wang Zuoqing, to return to their hometowns. 264 silver dollars were allocated. 144 Jiangxi famine refugees, including Liu Liji, and 31 Hebei famine refugees, including Liu Zhutian, were also assisted to return to their hometowns, with 234 yuan and 80 cents being allocated. 2. The association appointed Baker as an advisor, Jin Shaowu as deputy director, Yang Zigong as director of investigation and distribution in Hebei Province, Gao Haifeng and Sun Xianqing as deputy directors, Li Zizhong as director of investigation and distribution in Henan Province, Guo Fangwu as deputy director, Feng Yangshan as observer in Zhejiang, and Cheng Yiqing as inspector in Jiangsu, requesting ratification. 3. Regarding the association's telegram requesting the implementation of the Disaster Relief Reserve Fund Law, the Ministry of Finance replied that it plans to postpone the proposed "allocation of seeds starting from January 1, 1931" in the original draft until 1935 to ensure comprehensive consideration. In addition to consulting with the Ministry of Interior to revise, it will be submitted to the Ministry for countersigning and distributed to the departments for review, replying for reference. The directors of investigation and distribution in various provinces reported on the progress of their work.

Matters for Discussion: Regarding how to prepare and distribute seeds for spring plowing in disaster areas, it was decided to appoint Huang Bodu, Huang Hanzhi, Li Dachao, Huang Yinzhou, Baker, Chu Huiseng, Jin Shaowu, Guan Chouzhi, and eight others to form a Seed Preparation and Distribution Research Committee, and to designate Chu Huiseng to convene it. Regarding the remaining sixteen famine relief requests, it was decided to wait until funds are available for distribution.

Donations: The representative of the municipal government, Li Dachao, reported that the 100,000 yuan or so in disaster relief funds obtained from the city-wide donations last year was entrusted by Mayor Wu to be reported to this association and immediately handed over to the association for use. However, since these relief funds were raised during the city-wide donations with equal emphasis on bandit and drought disasters, the distribution of the relief funds should still be based on the principle of equal division between bandit and drought disasters. This is now included with an attached statement.

Xu Talks About Agricultural Relief: According to Mr. Xu Shiying, the severity of the disasters in various provinces last year was unprecedented. The methods of preparing and distributing relief funds are that, in addition to labor-based relief being handled by the provincial authorities themselves by issuing public bonds, emergency relief is initiated by various charitable organizations and agencies in Shanghai to form this association for handling. These two types have now been gradually implemented. The last one is agricultural relief. Although the central government also pays close attention to agricultural relief, the disaster areas in various provinces have suffered severe disasters, and there is no grass on the farmland, let alone seeds. Now that winter is passing and spring is approaching, the need for seeds is very urgent. This association's preparation and distribution of seeds is of great significance and mission. Now that there is a research committee to design it, it may be able to do its best to design for the farmers.

Huangshan Relief Delegation Representative Xie Benli Arrives in Shanghai 96

Will Soon Visit Committee Chairman Xu to Plead for Disaster Victims

Huangshan in Southern Anhui, once obscure due to inconvenient transportation, has gained prominence since the opening of the Hangzhou-Huizhou highway. The Anhui Provincial Government, appreciating the mountain's serene scenery, decided to develop it into a scenic area for tourism. Consequently, the Huangshan Construction Committee was established, with Xu Shiying, Chairman of the National Relief Commission, appointed as the Chairman, responsible for planning and construction. After a year of work, the highway from She County to the foot of the mountain was opened to traffic after the Double Tenth Festival last year. This road connects to the Hangzhou-Huizhou, Wuhu-Tunxi, and other roads, allowing travelers from Nanjing, Wuhu, Shanghai, Hangzhou, and other places to make day trips. Thus, Huangshan became widely known. Unexpectedly, after the onset of winter, the Red bandits entrenched in Jiangxi and Fujian provinces were routed by the National Army and scattered. Among them, two groups led by Luo Binghui and Fang Zhimin fled along the Zhejiang border to southern Anhui, invading Huangshan. Consequently, all villages, large and small, within the mountain were devastated. Wherever the bandits went, homes were turned to ashes. The slightly wealthier villagers managed to escape elsewhere, but the majority of farmers, lacking resources, had to take their elderly and children to hide in the deep mountains and valleys. The plight of the displaced was beyond description. Although the bandits who entered the mountain have now fled, scattered soldiers still appear from time to time, preventing those who sought refuge from daring to return quickly. The villages are deserted, and the scene is desolate. Adding to the hardship, a severe drought last summer resulted in a complete failure of the autumn harvest. Following a disastrous year, the people suffered banditry. Countless villagers died by the sword or were left to perish in ditches. Recently, She County Magistrate Shi posted public notices throughout the villages to reassure the people. However, the food and clothing of the general farmers had already been looted by the bandits, and their utensils were destroyed. Returning would mean starvation or freezing to death. Moreover, rumors have not subsided, and alarms are still frequent.

Therefore, many people still live in makeshift shelters in the mountains, sleeping in caves, gathering ferns to stave off hunger, and using thatch for warmth. The village chiefs and Baojia heads, originally local intellectuals, were the most targeted by the bandits. Apart from those who escaped in advance, many were killed by the bandits. With the villages lacking leadership, it is even more difficult to resettle the displaced. Xie Benli, the Bao chief of Yang Village, styled Yipu, is known for his enthusiasm for local public welfare. Due to the severe bandit and drought disasters suffered by his village and surrounding villages, and witnessing the widespread suffering in this harsh winter, he came to Shanghai yesterday to plead for relief from Relief Committee Chairman Xu on behalf of the disaster victims, appealing for help to rescue the remaining people after the calamity and repair the devastation in the villages. Last summer, Xu visited the mountain to inspect the Huangshan construction. At that time, the desolation was not yet complete, and the bandit atmosphere had not yet arrived. However, the mountain villages' economy was already bankrupt, and the livelihood of the mountain people was already showing signs of exhaustion. Now, with repeated disasters, the people's lives are unbearable. Therefore, if you want to build Huangshan and prosper southern Anhui, the most important task at present is to appease the displaced and provide emergency relief to alleviate the suffering of the survivors. Xu has always been compassionate and concerned about the suffering of others. Therefore, he will surely express sympathy for Xie's efforts and appeals and generously provide relief supplies. Xie plans to visit the Shanghai office of the Relief Commission in the coming days to present the tragic situation of the affected villages in the mountain and plead for the lives of tens of thousands of disaster victims.

The Shanghai Buddhist Association, for the purpose of raising relief funds for disaster victims, yesterday sent a letter to temples and monasteries in the city. Chongming Sojourning Shanghai Students Association 100

Organization of the Chongqi Co-Governance Promotion Association

Second Board Meeting Held Yesterday

Rules and Preface Passed

Shanghai News reports that the Chongming Sojourning Shanghai Students Association, in order to carry out the Chongqi co-governance movement, convened its second board meeting yesterday afternoon and passed the preface and organizational rules. Details are as follows:

Board Meeting Attendees: Yang Zhenzhong, Shi Chongpeng, Song An, Chen Dongbai, Tong Muge, Lu Yinpu, Chen Xiangxin, Gong Pixiong, etc. Chairman: Yang Zhenzhong. Recorder: Chen Dongbai. Matters discussed: (1) Determining the organizational name of the Chongqi co-governance movement. Resolved: The name will be the Chongqi Co-Governance Promotion Committee. (2) Passing the organizational rules and preface of the Promotion Committee. (3) Appointing Director Shi Chongpeng to be responsible for drafting the declaration of the Promotion Committee's establishment. (4) Setting the establishment meeting for 1:00 PM on February 10th at Minli Girls' High School. (5) Appointing Cao Yinqiu as an honorary director of the Association.

Preface Chongqi's separation has lasted for seven years. The residents have opposed it from the beginning and have petitioned for correction for seven years. The reasons for the opposition are: first, the residents' consent was not obtained; second, the burden on the people was ignored, and taxes were increased; and third, Chongming has suffered huge damage, while Qidong has achieved no construction results. Numerous documents have been disclosed over the years, and those who have seen them know the details, and those who have heard them are familiar with them. Last November, Provincial Chairman Chen had already submitted a meeting decision to the heads of the four departments of civil affairs, finance, education, and construction for review. The head of the Department of Civil Affairs convened a meeting on the matter. It is hoped that this matter will be resolved, but the timing is uncertain. However, the damage has lasted for seven years. Our colleagues living abroad are deeply concerned about our hometown and hope that the co-governance will be resolved as soon as possible so that local affairs can be sorted out as soon as possible. Therefore, promoting Chongqi co-governance is a matter of great urgency. The Association has initiated the organization of the Chongqi Co-Governance Promotion Committee to be responsible for carrying it out, striving for its success, and ensuring that the fragmented situation can be restored to its former state as soon as possible. Furthermore, according to Sun Yat-sen's nation-building program, local autonomy should be based on the county as a unit. Our Chongming originally combined the inner and outer sands into one unit. Unduly dividing one unit into two has led to a sharp increase in taxes, and the people feel overwhelmed. The expansion of political expenses has hindered the progress of projects. Educational expenses are in arrears, and disturbances are frequent. Water conservancy is neglected, and droughts and floods occur frequently. Therefore, hastily dividing the area has hundreds of disadvantages and not a single advantage. We, the members of this Association, love our hometown with a patriotic heart and recognize that loving our hometown is the starting point for loving our country. We save our compatriots from fire and water, and ask the authorities for mediation. The righteousness is for the public good, and the responsibility is unavoidable. In addition to separate detailed rules, we hereby state the preface, for your common consideration.

Organizational Rules The organizational rules of the Chongqi Co-Governance Promotion Committee are as follows: (1) Name: The name of this association shall be the Chongqi Co-Governance Promotion Committee. (2) Purpose: The purpose of this association is to promote Chongqi co-governance and relieve the people's suffering. (3) Committee Members: In addition to the entire board of directors of the Chongming Sojourning Shanghai Students Association serving as ex officio members of this association, the association may, at its discretion, appoint one to nine representatives from fellow countrymen living abroad and local organizations to serve as members. (4) Organization: The association will have a chairman elected from among the members, and will have four sections for general affairs, publicity, planning, and communication. (5) Meetings: The association's meetings will not be held on a fixed schedule and will be convened by the chairman as needed. (6) Funding: The association's expenses will be raised by the members in various ways. (7) Address: The association's temporary address will be at the Chongming Sojourning Shanghai Students Association, No. 979 Chengdu Road, Zhabei, Shanghai.

The Case of Gong Shaoting Killing His Concubine Has Been Indicted

The Corpse Remains Buried in Its Original Place and Was Not Cut Into Three Sections 101

Gong Falsely Accused His Concubine of Running Away After the Fact

Gong Shaoting, the owner of the Gong Hongtai Construction Factory located at the Gongxing Bridge South Embankment on Baoxing Road in Zhabei, conspired with his new concubine, Ms. Hou, and his son-in-law, Shen Fufu, etc., to strangle his old concubine, Xie Aiqiao (i.e., Sister Aiqiao), on the evening of the twenty-first day of the third month of the lunar calendar in the twenty-second year of the Republic of China. Afterward, they dismembered the corpse. Only recently did the deceased's nephew, Xie Baolin, discover the previous situation and report it to the Shanghai Public Security Bureau Detective Team, which arrested Gong Shaoting, Ms. Gong Hou, and the male and female accomplices who helped move the corpse, Zhou Baoquan and Li Baosheng, etc., a total of four suspects, and sent them to the local court for interrogation and detention. At the same time, they escorted the arrested suspects to unearth Sister Aiqiao's headless corpse and sent it to the Zhenru Forensic Research Institute for examination. However, the head is still missing. Details have been reported previously. It is now learned that after Sister Aiqiao was murdered, Gong Shaoting feared that something might go wrong, so he secretly instructed Zhou Baoquan, the worker guarding the construction site, to call the fugitive Liu Guisheng and Li Baosheng, etc., to dig up the corpse at night and transport it to another place. However, Liu Guisheng and others only put the severed head into a burlap sack and filled another burlap sack with soil, posing as Sister Aiqiao's corpse, falsely claiming that it had been cut into three sections. In reality, they only cut off the head, and the corpse remained buried in its original place. At that time, Liu Guisheng and others placed the two burlap sacks in a row basket, covered them with wooden flowers and firewood (to disguise them), carried them out with a carrying pole. According to reports, the head was buried in the Zhu Jiazhai public cemetery. However, the contents were learned by a gang of local ruffians in the area, who extorted money from them. Gong Shaoting gave Zhou Baoquan sixty yuan, instructing him to use it to pay for the corpse removal. Liu Guisheng and Li Baosheng each received twenty yuan, the ruffians took ten yuan, and the remaining ten yuan was used to buy ingot paper for burning as offerings for four yuan, and another six yuan was used to buy fish and meat at the market to feed the small laborers at the construction site, to shut their mouths. The arrangements were quite thorough. Gong Shaoting was extremely cunning and, after murdering Sister Aiqiao, even posted a notice falsely accusing Sister Aiqiao of running away, and even offered a reward, to make people believe that she had actually fled. It is now learned that the court has concluded its investigation and has filed a public indictment against Gong Shaoting, Ms. Gong Hou, and others for premeditated murder. A public trial will be held soon.

Lao Baosheng Silver Shop Sues Female Con Artist 103

Accumulated Huge Debt for Goods

British Consulate Continues to Hear Case of British Woman Manufacturing Narcotics 104

Origin of More Than Three Thousand Dollars' Worth of Purchased Goods Unclear

Husband and Wife's Telegrams Suspicious

The case of the British woman, the wife of Johnson, a resident of No. 361 Fahua Road, being accused of illegally manufacturing narcotics in her residence was heard again by the British Consulate Police Court on Thursday afternoon. The defendant maintained that she was unaware of the narcotics manufacturing equipment in her residence. The defendant could not explain why her and her husband's circumstances improved so dramatically after they received assistance from a charity last year, suddenly renting a large house, buying a car, and hiring many servants. The defendant admitted that since the end of December, she had paid 800 yuan as part of the car purchase price, 780 yuan for two months' rent (December and January), 250 yuan for the first installment of car fees, 300 yuan for the first installment of furniture fees, 150 yuan for miscellaneous expenses, and 79 yuan for carpet fees. When her husband left Shanghai for England on December 11, he left only 650 yuan in cash, while the defendant's expenses for purchasing goods totaled more than 3,014 yuan. Subsequently, the prosecutor presented telegrams exchanged between the defendant and her husband after the incident. In a telegram from the defendant to her husband, there was a sentence stating "The servant unauthorizedly manufactured flammable materials and caused a fire." The prosecutor argued that the defendant did not directly mention narcotics because she was trying to cover up the truth, knowing that her husband would understand that the narcotics manufacturing equipment had been discovered. In a telegram from the defendant's husband, there was "Feng gave 100 pounds," and another telegram contained "The mainland is backing you." The prosecutor said that reading these telegrams revealed subtle clues, clearly showing that the defendant knew about the narcotics manufacturing. The prosecutor questioned the defendant for a long time that day and finally asked the court to order the defendant to hand over a telegram that she claimed to have lost. The magistrate then adjourned the court and scheduled the hearing to continue on Monday.

The Number of Poor People at the Shanghai South Relief Center Has Increased Dramatically in Recent Days 106

Totaling Two Thousand Six Hundred and Thirteen People

Please Help with Expenses as Much as Possible

Since its opening, the Shanghai South Relief Center, established for winter relief for the poor, has seen a continuous increase in the number of people it houses. A reporter from the Guomin News visited the center at 1:00 PM yesterday, and was cordially received by Director Zhang Zixin, who led the reporter inside to inspect the poor. Although these people are homeless and destitute civilians, the order is very calm. Director Zhang also provided a detailed account of the center's overall situation, stating that the relief center is established every winter. The preparations began with a meeting of various charities convened by the Shanghai Charity Federation, following a letter from the Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau and under the supervision of benefactors such as Wang Yiting and Huang Hanzhi of the Federation. In accordance with established practice, the relief center was established in the South Shanghai area to house poor people without clothing or food. This year, the center was opened early at the Chaozhou Guild Hall at the South Railway Station, and a second center was established at the Chao Hui Villa on Xietu Road. At the beginning of the preparations, local gentry and merchants, such as Zhang Xiaoliang, were consulted to solicit large batches of planks from major lumber merchants and hire craftsmen to build sheds and other complete renovations. The internal organization is divided into management, accounting, general affairs, storage, supply, accommodation, registration, inspection, sanitation, and security. The staff members are selected and appointed by the chairman of the committee. Since the reception began on December 1st of last year, the number of poor people housed has reached 2,613 in both locations. The weather is suddenly cold, and more people are crowding in. When registering poor people, they are first questioned in detail, and their age, origin, occupation, and address (if any) are carefully investigated and filled in on the registration form. Then, a symbol is issued, their hair is shaved, they are bathed, and they are given accommodation and supplies. A set of winter clothes is issued, and their bodies are examined. If they are found to be addicted to opium or other diseases, they are sent to the city's drug rehabilitation center or given opium leaves daily to help them quit, or they are sent to various charity clinics for treatment. The poor are given three meals a day, two porridge and one rice, and vegetarian dishes. Currently, about 20 shi of rice are needed for daily meals. The poor are managed in groups of twelve, with one person with some knowledge selected as the group leader. Two people share one bed in the dormitory, and quilts are provided completely. During meals and lodging, they must obey the command of the group leader and be managed by the administrators in rotation. The emphasis is on supervision and guidance. Police officers are sent by the Public Security Bureau to maintain order among the poor. Once the weather warms up in the spring, they will be sent away in batches, either with money or with train and ship tickets to return to their hometowns, or sent to relevant charitable organizations for education, care, and relief. However, due to various difficulties in managing, supplying, and funding, the center has not been able to establish a separate female center to house and relieve women and children in poverty, and feels that this is a regrettable shortcoming. The center has no dedicated funds and relies entirely on fundraising to support itself. Currently, in addition to the subsidies allocated by the city government, benefactors and charities have donated more than 16,000 yuan. All income and expenditure are carefully managed, and reports are prepared and submitted to the chairman of the committee for review every ten days, and funds are withdrawn from the Federation in installments for actual expenditure and verification. A report will be compiled and printed for distribution to various sectors of society for creditworthiness. The center strives for openness and hopes that all sectors will provide more guidance.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Submits to Municipal Government Again 108

Requesting Reduction in Medicine and Liquor License Tax

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce submitted a document to the municipal government yesterday, stating: "Regarding the continuation of the submission based on the facts: It has been found that the Shanghai National Medicine Trade Association requested a reduction or exemption of the medicine and liquor license tax and the return of the fine from Lao Lai Yi. This matter was forwarded by your subordinate association to your office, document number 2471, which disapproved the request. After the record of the disapproval was circulated and made known, the National Medicine Trade Association submitted a letter to this association, stating roughly that complete exemption of the medicine and liquor license tax is difficult to obtain. However, it has been found that the medicine and liquor tax has been divided into two types, four yuan and two yuan. The municipal government has approved that the over-collection of eight yuan for those who originally paid four yuan be corrected according to the regulations. There will be no further conflicts. However, those who originally paid two yuan are all small-scale, with few customers, struggling to avoid hunger and cold, barely maintaining operations, like walking on thin ice. Recently, they have been even more affected by the economic downturn. Moreover, their numbers are limited. The increase of two yuan by the municipal government is not much, but for these businesses, these two yuan are more than tens of millions for the wealthy. Their economic capacity is very fragile. In addition to forwarding the municipal government's instructions to all Chinese members for compliance, a special document has been prepared to request the municipal government to show compassion for the difficulties of businesses and show mercy beyond the law. All Chinese medicine and liquor license taxes should maintain the original status and continue to be collected in two types, four yuan and two yuan, to show consideration and facilitate survival, etc. According to this, it has been found that Chinese medicine stores also sell medicine and liquor for treatment, which is different from those who specialize in selling alcohol for consumption. This has been described in detail in previous submissions from your subordinate association. It is now said that the Chinese medicine stores in the Chinese area that hold two-yuan licenses are all small-scale businesses. If the tax is doubled, it will be difficult to support, which is true. The request to keep the Chinese medicine and liquor license tax at the original status, divided into two levels of four yuan and two yuan, is indeed for the sake of the majority of small-scale businesses. It is reasonable to continue to submit this matter based on the facts. We hope that your office will review and approve this matter and order the Finance Bureau to approve the request for the sake of public convenience. Sincerely submitted."

Gradual Improvement in Domestic Cement 109

Strong Sales and Rising Prices

Guangdong's Implementation of Control Affects Trade

China's cement industry was severely declining due to the dumping of cement by Japan and Russia. Since the government increased import tariffs, foreign loans have become more expensive and imports have decreased. The business has gradually improved. The details are as follows:

Sales Have Improved According to people in the cement industry yesterday, China's cement industry has long been manipulated by Japan and Russia, resulting in a sharp drop in market prices and sluggish sales. Since the government increased cement import tariffs last year, foreign loans have become more expensive and imports have decreased sharply. Domestic cement has gradually improved. Since the beginning of winter, sales have been particularly strong. The daily sales volume is generally more than 1,500 barrels. The monthly output of cement companies such as Qixing in North China, Longtan in Jiangsu Province, and China Merchants is often insufficient to supply demand. The current selling price per barrel is six yuan, an increase of 20-30% compared to the past. There is a possibility of further price increases in the future.

Guangdong Implements Control Recently, in order to develop the industry in the province, Guangdong Province has implemented control over the cement trade, stipulating that buildings worth more than 10,000 yuan must purchase the province's Five Rams brand cement. As a result, cement produced in other provinces has no possibility of being sold. This province is a cement-producing area, and its foreign trade has been severely affected. Since the second half of last year, no cement has been transported from this city to Guangdong for sale.
