County Government Returns Public Security Loans 112

The Shanghai County Public Security expenses for October of the 18th year of the Republic of China were difficult to raise because the municipal funds were suspended. During the tenure of the former county magistrate Lu, the district offices were ordered to raise loans on behalf of the public security bureau, which issued stamped receipts. Later, because the funds of the branch bureaus were insufficient, the districts were again ordered to guarantee and borrow firewood and rice from the stores. Except for the store accounts and temporary advances, which have been repaid in installments from the remaining public security funds by the county government, the remaining loan portion has not yet been repaid. The district chiefs have previously submitted a report requesting repayment. Now, the Finance Department has ordered that the repayment be made from the remaining county tax funds for the 22nd year of the Republic of China. As this fundraising is mostly collected in small amounts, formal receipts are required before payment can be made. Therefore, the county government yesterday instructed the district offices to collect all the original receipts from the creditors and send them to the county as proof for the district to forward the payment.

Engineer Gao Gongmao of Shunchang Stone Powder Factory Was Kidnapped and Escaped 113

The person himself sent a telegram from Ningbo saying that he had escaped and was returning to his hometown

The family members were half-convinced and went to inquire

Gao Gongmao, an engineer at the Shunchang Stone Powder Factory and Iron Factory in Zhoujiadu, was kidnapped on the morning of the 19th of this month. At 10:00 a.m., he and the factory owner Ma Xiongguan were traveling in their own car to the issuing office. When they were passing in front of the St. Mary's Girls' School on Bailinan Road, they were suddenly ambushed by four bandits. The bandits threw a bicycle in front of the car to block the way. Then they jumped into the car and showed their pistols. Since the factory owner Ma Xiongguan was wearing worker's clothing, he was driven down. Instead, the engineer Gao Gongmao was kidnapped. After driving for about a mile, the bandits also drove the driver down and drove away themselves. The next day, the car was found at the intersection of Xiai Xians Road and Ladu Road in the French Concession. After the incident, the factory owner and Gao's family reported the case to the Public Security Bureau and the Jing'an Temple Road Police Station, requesting a thorough investigation. The details have been reported previously. After the case occurred, the authorities in the Chinese and French Concessions attached great importance to it. Although they tried their best to investigate, they could not find any clues. To this day, Gao's whereabouts are unknown, and there has been no letter from the bandits, making the investigation even more difficult. Unexpectedly, Gao's wife, Shi Lanxuan, (who works as a clerk in the Toyota Yarn Factory in Fanhuangdu) suddenly received a telegram from Gao Gongmao from her hometown in Qianpai Xuan, Xinchang County, Zhejiang Province, the day before yesterday (the 24th), stating: "Shanghai Fanhuangdu Toyota Yarn Factory Shi Lanxuan, I passed Ningbo yesterday and arrived safely in Xin, tell Shunchang, Gongmao." After receiving the telegram, Shi was surprised and delighted, but also half-convinced. In addition to reporting to the Shunchang Iron Factory, she also sent the telegram to the Caojiadu Branch Bureau for instructions. After detailed study, they believed that the telegram needed to be verified. Therefore, at noon the day before yesterday, Shi sent a telegram to Xinchang to inquire about the truth from her father-in-law Gao Yunjie. At about 8:00 a.m. yesterday morning, she received another telegram from Gao Gongmao in Xinchang, stating: "Shanghai Fanhuangdu Toyota Yarn Factory Shi Lanxuan, I arrived home safely this afternoon, Mao." Therefore, Shi also sent this telegram to the Caojiadu Branch Bureau for reporting. After reviewing the telegram, Director Wang Dasui of the bureau ordered Geng Shoubao, the leader of the detective squad stationed in the bureau, to appoint detectives Zhong Xuehuai and Zhu Bengui to take their passports and official documents and rush to Xinchang on the Ning Shao Company's commercial ship last night to meet Gao and investigate the truth of Gao's escape for reporting purposes. Gao's wife, Shi Lanxuan, also went with them. It is expected that the truth will be revealed soon.

Xinzha Police Station Uncovers Two Heroin Manufacturing Sites 114

Profit-seeking People Fear No Law

One Falls, Another Rises, Impossible to Catch Them All

The public security authorities of the Public Concession have recently been cracking down on drugs, and large-scale operations involving red pills and morphine are frequently uncovered. Smaller-scale operations are uncovered almost daily. However, those who profit from this are fearless of the law. They rise one after another. There is no end to catching them. The day before yesterday, Chinese Detective Mao Yiwen and Western Detective Bao Taibo of the Xinzha Police Station uncovered two large heroin manufacturing sites in the Chinese and French Concessions. The details of the case are recorded below:

Han Debao from Zhejiang, also known as Zhao Jinsun, has been making a lot of money from operating drugs. He lives at No. 4 Juxian Village, Lane 116, Kangnuo Road (Chinese Area). He usually lives a luxurious life, employs many servants, and buys his own car for transportation. The concession number is 13162. Han has recently realized that manufacturing drugs can make a lot of money, and it is more profitable than other industries. Therefore, he rented a semi-Western-style house at No. 11 1/2 Huangjiasha Garden, Block B, Xinzha, from the China Business Company on Sichuan Road, for a monthly rent of about 80 taels of silver. He set up machines, hired male and female workers, and worked day and night to manufacture the most poisonous heroin for private sale. This was discovered by Chinese Detective Mao Yiwen of the Xinzha Police Station. He reported the matter to the First Special Court and obtained a search warrant. At about 4:00 a.m. the day before yesterday, he, together with Chinese Detective Yang Peizhang, Ruan Yao, and Western Detective Bao Tai, secretly went to No. 11 1/2 Huangjiasha Garden and arrested nine male and female workers, including (1) Wang Gengsheng from Jiangbei, (2) Cai Qiugen from Pudong, (3) Zhou Jinqiu from Shaoxing, (4) Wo Gengsheng from Ningbo, (5) Wang Agen from Jiangbei, (6) Tian Xilin from Shaoxing, (7) Madam Zhou Zhao, (8) He Jumei, (9) Du Qiao'e, all from Shaoxing. They seized six large packages of opium, totaling 53 pounds, 84 taels of heroin powder, five account books, two seals, and contracts. Later, the arrested criminals confessed that the boss of this case was Han Debao and led the Chinese and Western detectives and detectives from the Sixth District Public Security Bureau to No. 4 Juxian Village, Kangnuo Road, where Han was arrested. Forty-seven taels of morphine were seized, along with his wife Han Wu, Wang Xiangjin, Wang Wu, Wang Xiankang, and five others, as well as a car. They were all taken to the Sixth District Public Security Bureau for temporary detention, pending transfer. Yesterday morning, the police station first sent the nine male and female criminals, including Wang Gengsheng, who were arrested in the concession, to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special Court for prosecution in accordance with Article 6 of the Anti-Smoking Law. Zhang Tianyin, the police station's lawyer, rose to state the circumstances of the case, saying that the police station arrested the nine defendants in No. 11 1/2 Huangjiasha Garden. When the investigators arrived, one or two defendants jumped out of the window and climbed onto the roof. The first defendant, Wang Gengsheng, fell into a lower roof due to panic and was captured. The second defendant, Cai Qiugen, was arrested by the investigators on the roof. According to the confessions of the one or two defendants, this operation was controlled by Han Debao, who lives at No. 4 Kangnuo Road. Han came to this operation once a day to guide the dispensing and manufacturing methods. After the heroin was made, he took it away. The third, fourth, fifth, sixth, and fourth defendants were workers, and the seventh, eighth, and ninth, three female defendants were maids. After seizing the above-mentioned items, they went to No. 4 Juxian Village, Kangnuo Road, together with the Sixth District Public Security Bureau. When they arrived, the double doors were tightly closed. After the investigators knocked on the door for a long time, the tenth defendant, Han Debao, also escaped to the roof of No. 1 next door. After being captured, the twelfth defendant, Wang Xiangjin, opened the door, and a total of five people were arrested. Forty-seven taels of morphine and a car were seized. They are now all in the Sixth District Public Security Bureau. They requested the court to prepare a document so that they could be transferred. The police station requested permission to reschedule the case and asked the court to go to the scene for inspection to clarify the truth. The seized opium and heroin were presented to the court. The remaining machines and other items were not brought because they were inconvenient to carry. When questioned, all the defendants confessed that they were hired by Han Debao. Judge Liu Yugui ordered that the case be rescheduled for next Wednesday. The four defendants, six, seven, eight, and nine, who had minor offenses, were allowed to be released on bail of 20 yuan each, while the others were detained. It was decided to go to No. 11 1/2 Huangjiasha Garden for inspection at 3:00 p.m. today.

Six Shipping Companies on the Shanghai-Hankou Line Are Resuming Alliance and Cooperation 115

In View of Intense Competition and Drastic Drop in Water Transport Prices

Negotiating the Implementation of Shared Water Transport Prices

Six shipping companies operating on the Shanghai-Hankou line in the lower reaches of the Yangtze River, such as the state-run China Merchants Bureau, the private Sanbei, Ningshao, British Taikoo, Yihai, and Japanese Nisshin, had signed an agreement to form an alliance and cooperate to implement shared water transport prices before the Shanghai War. After the dissolution, the companies competed fiercely, resulting in a drastic drop in water transport prices. Now, the companies have realized this deeply and are planning to resume the alliance and cooperation. They are currently negotiating separately, and it is expected that a formal meeting will be held after the end of the accounting period to make a decision.

Yongji and Other Three Ships of Dazhen Company Have Been Taken Back for Self-operation 116

Preparing to Participate in the Shanghai-Hai Line Water and Land Intermodal Transport

Please Contact the Industry Association and the China Merchants Bureau for Negotiations

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, after the state-run China Merchants Bureau implemented water and land cargo intermodal transport with the Longhai Railway, the cargo along the line was transferred from the Lao Yao Wharf, and the cargo at the Dapu Wharf decreased sharply. The Dazhen Shipping Company, which operates between Shanghai and Dapu, has leased all its ships, Yongji (1,847 tons), Yongping (1,421 tons), and Yongan (1,421 tons), to the China Merchants Bureau for a period of eight months. Now that the term has expired, Dazhen Company has decided to take them back. The Yongping has been returned a few days ago and entered the dock for annual major repairs. The Yongji is scheduled to be returned at the end of the month, and the Yongan is scheduled to be returned on the 15th of next month. The company has decided to operate the Shanghai-Lianyungang line, because it has been approved by the Ministry of Railways and the Ministry of Communications to participate in the Shanghai-Hai line intermodal transport. The Shanghai Shipping Industry Association is currently negotiating with the China Merchants Bureau. If the issue of Yongping participating in intermodal transport after repairs has not been resolved, it is decided to temporarily operate the Shanghai-Fuzhou line.

Chairman Chiang Kai-shek Advocates the Use of Han Regular Script Movable Type Edition 117

The Han Regular Script Movable Type Edition was created by the Han Regular Script Printing Bureau on Shandong Road in this city. The font is neat and the strokes are beautiful. It is a new era in Chinese printing tools. Therefore, the popularity of regular script printing has been widespread in recent years. The documents directly printed by the bureau are no less than 40,000 to 50,000 types, such as the Railway Yearbook, the National Bank Yearbook, and the National Salt Administration Records. All the macro-volumes are printed with this movable type. More than 360 printing houses in China have changed to or also print the Han Regular Script Movable Type Edition due to social demand. Recently, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek considered this Han Regular Script Movable Type Edition to be popular and beautiful, and the regular script has an extremely important position in Chinese cultural history and has been the script used by the nation for thousands of years. Promoting the inherent culture and popularizing mass education require the promotion of regular script printing. Therefore, he ordered the subordinate agencies to adopt it uniformly to promote and spread it widely.

Suzhou River Was Open to Navigation Yesterday 119

The Suzhou River has been reported in the newspapers recently due to the shallow water in the river and the excessive number of ships passing through, resulting in the interruption of navigation. It is now known that since Xu Zunian, the patrol officer of the Second Water Patrol Division of the Public Security Bureau, led the police to find ways to dredge the river for several days, as of yesterday afternoon, although there has been navigation for two days and nights, it is still temporarily opened and closed due to the excessive number of ships. Officer Xu believed that this would not be a proper solution, so at about 3:00 p.m. yesterday, he called the headquarters and asked the First Division to order the ships to be blocked from entering the river with ropes at the Waibaidu Bridge, because it was high tide at that time, and the original ships in the river were allowed to sail westward with the tide, so the navigation was completely opened at about 6:00 p.m.

Li Meiying Sues for Mediation and Divorce from Wei Yifei

Detailed Account of Wei's Absurd Behavior

The Mother-in-Law Has Three Nicknames

The woman Li Meiying, also known as Wei Li, is twenty-four years old, from Ningbo, and currently resides at No. 36 Jiugeng Lane, Miller Road, Hongkou. She was previously married to Wei Yifei (twenty-eight years old, from Shaoxing, owner of Shiyi Bakery and part-time actor in film companies), currently residing at No. 160 at the intersection of Beile Road and Avenue Joffre in the French Concession. Recently, due to a breakdown in the marital relationship, Li hired lawyer Chen Wenxiang to file a petition with the Civil Mediation Office of the Second Special Court, accusing her husband of abuse and abandonment, requesting mediation for divorce, and seeking alimony, etc. Upon receiving the petition, the court, yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, convened both parties to the Seventh Tribunal for mediation, presided over by Judge Li Liang. The petitioner, Li Meiying, stated that she was married to the respondent through a matchmaker on the second day of the ninth lunar month in the eighteenth year of the Republic. Only after the marriage did she discover that he

indulges in gambling and prostitution, does not engage in proper work, and only makes a living by acting in movies. When she advised him, not only did he not change, but he harbored resentment and frequently subjected her to beatings and insults over the years. Moreover, her mother-in-law aided and abetted his wrongdoing, and resented her for having too few dowry gifts, often saying she wanted her son to remarry. During the January 28th Incident, the respondent's business flourished, and he purchased a car, becoming even more absurd. He secretly rented a house with the prostitute Shi Fanglaoqi, and contracted syphilis, which he transmitted to her, causing her third child to be born with sores all over the body and die after a little over ten days. After breaking up with Shi Fanglaoqi, he took in Chunqiulaoqi as a singer, renting a house for her at No. 40 Xixiang Lane, Sichuan Road, spending four or five thousand gold coins. Later, he had an affair with the prostitute Tao Yahong Ajiu, spending tens of thousands of gold. As a result, Chunqiulaoqi resented his

infidelity and filed a lawsuit in court, costing several thousand more gold coins. The petitioner, concerned about his extravagant spending and the risk of contracting syphilis, repeatedly cried and pleaded with him, but to no avail. In the winter of the twenty-second year, the respondent, taking advantage of her returning home to visit her mother, moved away all the rosewood furniture from the house. Knowing his ill intentions, the woman sternly questioned him, but he saw her as a thorn in his side. On May 2nd of this year, the respondent tried to move her clothes trunk unsuccessfully and even stabbed her with a knife. She then reported to the police station, and he left and never returned. A few weeks later, she encountered him on the street and questioned him, only to be beaten again. She reported the abuse to the police three times. The respondent, through his mother and brother-in-law Chen Kaihua, etc.,

lured her into divorce, offering to pay her silver dollars four thousand five hundred. The woman couldn't bear it and hoped that the respondent would repent and change his ways, so she listened to their advice and let it go. However, since then, he only occasionally came home during the day and never stayed overnight. The woman's tolerance was based on the importance she placed on the marital bond. In mid-December of last year, the respondent decided to reduce her monthly allowance from fifty yuan to thirty yuan. When she refused, he started creating trouble every day. On December 30th, the woman returned home to visit her mother and then went to the theater with her older sister to relieve her depression. Upon returning home from the theater at night, the respondent, believing he had an opportunity, falsely accused the petitioner of misconduct outside the home, locked the door, and refused to let her in. The petitioner had no choice but to return to her mother's home and cry. Later, despite repeated persuasion from relatives, the respondent insisted on forcing a divorce and neglected his two young children. Under such circumstances, he showed

no kindness and intended to abandon her, so she requested alimony of fifteen thousand yuan, and the return of clothes, jewelry, and the educational expenses for the two children, etc. The respondent Wei Yifei did not appear in court. His lawyer stated that the petitioner had been exceptionally shrewish since marrying the respondent, and even the mother-in-law and sisters-in-law were afraid of her. The neighbors all knew this, and her associates were all unemployed hooligans, so the respondent dared not appear in court today. Last month, the petitioner claimed to return to Ningbo and went to a

dance hall with an unknown young man. After dancing, they went to a hotel in Hongkou. The next day, she returned home, and the respondent had collected evidence and was about to file a lawsuit. Instead, the petitioner preemptively framed him. All her claims are completely false, etc. Li Meiying also said that her mother-in-law was a notorious female tiger. After the woman married into the family, she slept in the woman's room every night. She took a bath every day in the summer, and every time she bathed, she made the woman scrub her back. After bathing, she sat on a stool to cool off, completely naked. When the woman told her to put on her pants, not only did she not listen, but she was scolded. The mother-in-law had three nicknames: Female Tiger, Twelve O'Clock, and Crazy. At this point, the court declared the mediation unsuccessful and ordered the petitioner to file a formal lawsuit, then adjourned the court.

Xie Xiaochu Discusses the Monopoly of Sulfuric Acid and Nitric Acid in Jiangsu Province 125

Recently, Western newspapers have repeatedly reported news about the Ministry of Finance regarding sulfuric acid and nitric acid. According to Xie Xiaochu, a member of the City Chamber of Commerce, the monopoly of sulfuric acid and nitric acid in Jiangsu Province began in April of the twenty-first year and was handled by the Tongxing Company under the commission of the Jiangsu Provincial General Office for Nitric and Sulfuric Acid Transportation and Sales. A surplus profit of one dollar per box was collected. Now, the contract between the Jiangsu Provincial General Office for Nitric and Sulfuric Acid Transportation and Sales and the Jiangsu Provincial General Bureau of Nitric and Sulfuric Acid is expiring at the end of this month. The Jiangsu Provincial General Bureau of Nitric and Sulfuric Acid, in view of the importance of sulfuric and nitric acid to industry, and for the convenience of management, has taken it back and presented it to the Ministry of Finance for direct invitation of merchants to contract. Currently, there are rumors from various sectors that I am contracted to handle it, which is a misunderstanding. Although I am engaged in the chemical raw materials business, I am very busy with many affairs, and my time and energy are difficult to spare. Yesterday, I met with Huang Chundao, the director of the Jiangsu Provincial General Bureau of Nitric and Sulfuric Acid, who said that Lei Runqin, the founder of Huaan Chemical Factory, has been commissioned to take over the handling, and will take office on February 1st. The surplus profit will remain the same, with one dollar per box collected.

Pig Butchers Request Abolition of Slaughtering Fee 128

Social Bureau Rejects Request

In this city's fresh pork butchering industry, when pigs are collected from the pigpens, a slaughtering fee must be paid. Last December, the pig butchering industry suddenly raised objections, petitioning party and government agencies to request its abolition, and requesting the assistance of the City Chamber of Commerce, which led to opposition from the pigpens and caused disputes. The city party headquarters summoned them for mediation. Now, the case has been reviewed by the Social Bureau based on the facts, and the pig butcher's request to abolish the slaughtering fee has been rejected.

The Changxing Wheel of the Sanbei Company discovered smuggled opium on board on its return to Shanghai from Hankou. The person carrying it was arrested. The details are as follows:

Ship Searched: The Hankou authorities are very strict in searching for smuggling when ships leave. Since the ban on opium, the prevention of opium smuggling has been even stricter. A special opium suppression inspectorate has been formed to be in charge of searching. When the Jianglun ships of each company are launched, they must be searched, regardless of the coal ship or the fire cabin. When the Changxing Wheel of the Sanbei Company left Hankou, it was on Tuesday. As the ship was sailing, a team of opium suppression inspectors boarded the ship to search. It seemed that they had received a tip-off, so they searched every place.

Opium Seized: The staff of the Opium Suppression Inspectorate first searched the cabins but found nothing. Later, they searched the fire cabin but found nothing. Finally, they searched the coal cabin near the machine and seized a bag of smuggled opium. It was said to contain five or six hundred taels. After the inspection team seized the opium, they searched again, because they received a tip that there was more than one bag of smuggled opium. But after a thorough search, no second batch was found. They took the seized opium and began investigating the person carrying it.

Captain Arrested: After the opium was discovered, the person responsible for smuggling the opium was investigated. All the crew members and porters said they did not know anything. Finally, after questioning by the inspectors, it was discovered that a cook in the small galley of the ship was suspected of smuggling. The cook was arrested on the spot and taken ashore to the inspectorate for interrogation. The Changxing Wheel was then allowed to sail to Shanghai. After the ship arrived in Shanghai, the captain, Jiao Dingxi, went to the bureau yesterday to report to the director the situation of the opium seizure and the arrest of the cook.

Sentencing for Human Trafficking 130

Xu Yin, a woman from Liyang, due to the famine there last September, brought her daughters Jin Di, twelve years old, and Yi Di, eight years old, to Shanghai to sell to Che Guo, a woman from Taizhou, No. 45 Tongchang Lane, Haining Road, for 125 yuan, to Wu Zhang, No. 373 Tongchang Lane, and Ji Jinhai, No. 365 Qiujiang Road, Zhabei, as daughters-in-law. There was a contract. Recently, a fellow villager, Ruan Mugen, learned of this way to make a living and also brought his six-year-old younger sister, Tong Di, and his six-year-old niece, Zhang Su Di, to Shanghai to be sold by Che Guo. Zhang Su Di was taken out by a fellow villager named Xiao Jinzi, and could not be found. Ruan Tong Di was told by Che Guo and her cohabiting Cantonese woman Chen A Gu to Qi Gu, a Cantonese woman in nearby Dexing Lane, that the price was 62 yuan to be an adopted daughter, and a deposit of 2 yuan was paid first. While this was in progress, Xu Yongyuan, a Chinese detective from the Hongkou Police Station, and detectives Zhang Yunsheng and Chen Dabao, learned of the situation and, in coordination with Western detectives, went to Tongchang Lane at 2:30 PM on the 13th of this month and arrested Xu Yin, Ruan Mugen, Che Guo, the main offender, Che Yongkang, her lover, the Cantonese woman Chen A Gu, and others. They also rescued the Liyang girls Yin Xiao Litou, twelve years old (who was brought from her hometown by Xu Yin to stay with her), Ruan Tong Di, Xu Jin Di, and Yi Di, and sent them to the First Special District Court for interrogation. All these details have been reported in this newspaper. Yin Xiao Litou and the other four girls were sent to the Women and Children's Relief Association for care. Yesterday morning, Judge Xiao Xie-fen visited the Third Criminal Court and thoroughly investigated the defendants, sentencing Che Guo to two years and four months in prison, Ruan Mugen to seven months in prison, and Chen A Gu to six months in prison, with a three-year suspended sentence. Che Yongkang and Xu Yin were acquitted and released.

Autopsy on Apprentice Who Died from Drinking Poisonous Water 131

The Xinhe Electroplating Machinery Factory at No. 40, Lvsheng Lane, Dongyouheng Road, is owned by Chen Ruisheng, a native of Ningbo. On the afternoon of the previous day, around 6:00 PM, an apprentice named Sun Zhaofa, fifteen years old, also a native of Ningbo, felt dissatisfied with his work and, in a fit of resentment, took his own life by secretly drinking potassium cyanide solution used for electroplating. He was found by his companion Shi Daihe, who saw him moaning on the ground and immediately informed the shop owner. He was sent to Tongren Hospital for treatment, but it was ineffective, and he died soon after. The hospital reported it to the Huishan Police Station, which ordered detective Ji Peijin to investigate. The body was taken to the Feilun Road mortuary. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Court commissioned Prosecutor Guo Wei, along with medical examiner Zhang Yan and clerk Wang Zuyi, to go to the mortuary to examine the body. According to Hua Butou Shen Baoshan, Sun Zhaofa had said he had been treated unfairly. Shi Daihe testified that he was from Shaoxing, twelve years old, and also an apprentice in the factory. The deceased had told him that he was very dissatisfied with his work and was afraid that his father would blame him when he returned home. Last night, he saw him fall to the ground. The boss had not beaten him. Sun Yongzheng, the father of the deceased, also submitted a statement. Guo Jun ordered the examination to confirm that Sun Zhaofa, male, died from drinking potassium cyanide poison. The body was handed over to his father, Sun Yongzheng, who signed a receipt and took it back for burial.

Child Dies in Lime Kiln Fire 134

Jia Jingcai's Baby Dies Tragically

At around 8:10 AM yesterday, a thatch shed with no address in the lime kiln of Xiaoshadu, Western Shanghai, the home of Jia Jingcai from Danyang, carelessly started a fire while cooking, and the accumulated firewood suddenly caused a thick smoke to spread and penetrate the roof. In an instant, it spread to the neighbors on the left and right. The fire brigade quickly drove to the scene and extinguished the fire. A total of three thatched sheds were burned down. When the fire was raging, Jia Jingcai and his wife, Ms. Du, were eager to escape and forgot to take out their newborn baby, who had not yet reached one month old, resulting in her being buried and burned to death in the fire. Officer Gu of the Roberts Road Police Substation sent police officers to investigate and arrested and sent Jia Jingcai and his wife to the Caojiadu Substation for questioning.

Little West Heaven 143

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 8: A Remote and Simple Official Quickly Issues a Strong Decree; Outside the Magnificent Hall, There Are Pitiful Creatures

This is truly a malpractice. I heard that my predecessor used twenty-four debt collectors. Cheng Zhiqian couldn't help but laugh when he heard this. Zhou Yourong said, "Brother Zhiqian, do you think I'm lying?" Zhiqian laughed, "I'm not laughing at you for lying, I'm laughing at your limited view. There's a county in Gansu where there are one hundred and twenty-eight debt collectors. This number isn't just a rumor, it's an unofficial announcement. So, what's the big deal about twenty or thirty debt collectors?" Zhou Yourong said to Jiefu, "Listen to what kind of government this is? As a magistrate, you have no other task than to scrape money from the people. If they don't have money, you force them to their death. If they squeeze out money, you hand it over to the local garrison with both hands. Education, justice, construction, nothing can be discussed." Jiefu said, "How can justice not be discussed? Are the people so poor that they can't even afford lawsuits?" Zhou Yourong said, "Of course they are. They have problems even getting food. What lawsuits can they file? Even if there are lawsuits, and you decide on a crime, the commander can send a groom to take the person away. You've wasted your effort. Conversely, if the people offend the commander, and he doesn't want to hand them over to the military court, they send them to the county. The magistrate has to follow orders with the utmost care. If you don't, the groom will slap the county magistrate in the face. The emperor is far away, where can you go to complain about injustice? But I'm different. I came here with the orders of the provincial government. I won't let them interfere with matters within my yamen. There have been several conflicts, but they didn't dare to openly kill me, so they had to back down." Jiefu said, "Since the local commander backed down, why did Magistrate Zhou quit?" Zhou Yourong stomped his feet and jumped up, saying, "It's unbearable! Two recent incidents made it impossible for me to continue. Once, a merchant came from another county, probably very rich. He was arrested by the Eighth Master and taken to the city wall. They hung him up and beat him to force him to give money. They never got the money and strangled him to death, throwing him off the city wall. Of course, the county magistrate is responsible for an unidentified corpse on the ground." (122)

Talking About Deer 144

— Lü Mengjiao

Deer are produced in the mountains and forests, and they are extremely docile. People in the past mostly used them as embellishments for gardens. Male deer have antlers, shaped like tree branches, which are quite beautiful. Females do not have antlers. Their fur is reddish-brown with white star-shaped spots, resembling plum blossoms, hence the common name "sika deer." There are many different kinds.

The antlers of male deer are like sprouts when they first grow, covered with skin. The swollen part of the skin is shaped like a mushroom, called deer velvet, which is a precious ingredient in medicine. The ones produced in the three eastern provinces are especially good, called "Northeast deer velvet." After the antlers grow, they branch out. They are shed and replaced every year, adding one branch each year, until they stop when they are old.

The Qing Yu Tang Pharmacy in Hangzhou was established very early and has a large scale. It raises dozens of deer inside, enclosed by iron fences, for people to browse. This is because they store medicinal materials. When I was young, I often went to see them with my ancestors, but the piles of urine and feces inside the enclosure made it impossible for viewers to stay for long.

Deer are easily startled. When they live in groups, they surround themselves with their antlers, forming a circle like a formation, to protect themselves from harm from people. See "Miscellaneous Notes of the Three Leftovers."

"New Qi Xie" says, "Lin'an produces deer. They give birth to their young around Qingming Festival. The young must wait for rain before they can walk. If there is no rain, they cannot walk at all. Scholars who find them take them home and feed them sheep's milk. When they grow up, they follow the sheep, called 'sheep-milk deer.'"

Old deer can grow jade in their antlers after many years, called "deer jade," also known as "deer jade." "Qing Wang Yingkui's Continuation of Willow South Notes" records, "Yu Chenglong was a Sima in Huangzhou. A wild man presented him with a dead deer, as tall as a horse, with large and mottled antlers. A silver ring was tied around its neck, weighing seventeen taels, engraved with the seven characters 'Huaqing Palace, Tianbao Second Year.' The bottom of the antlers was solid and transparent like jade, which is what is called 'deer jade.'"

Deer meat is delicious, but not easily obtained. Those who have eaten it say that its taste is far above that of roe deer meat. Its fur can be used to make brushes, hence the famous deer hair brushes.

"Meaning of the Rites of the Book of Rites" says that the people of Yizhou kill deer and bury them in the ground to let them rot, then take them out to eat. This is called "deer [unclear character]," also a strange way to eat deer.

Deer tails and deer tendons are both precious ingredients in dishes, but they are not easy to prepare well. "Suiyuan's Menu" once recorded the method of cooking deer tendons: "Deer tendons are difficult to soften. They must be pounded and boiled three days in advance, squeezing out the gamey water several times. Add meat broth to simmer them, then use chicken broth to simmer them. Add a little soy sauce and wine, thicken the sauce, and do not add anything else. They will become white and can be served on a plate. If you use ham, winter bamboo shoots, mushrooms, and bamboo shoots together to simmer them, they will become red and are served in a bowl without thickening the sauce. White ones should be sprinkled with fine peppercorn powder." Today, there are few who speak of the method of cooking deer, so I have recorded it in detail. Those who want to enjoy a delicious meal, why not try it?

Tidbits 145

Rich people talk about eating and drinking all day long, while poor people worry about eating and drinking all day long. That's life.

Wives: In the past, they were "inner helpers," but now they often become "inner troubles."

Students in schools are "imprisoned" in class every day, and teachers are "repaying debts." When the holidays come, it is when the students' "sentences" are over and the teachers' "debts" have been paid off.

Five Mounds Six Families Village 146

— Sleeping Buddha

"Five Mounds Six Families Village, wives support men,"

"Men gamble with cards, women carry salt to sell,"

"Five Mounds Six Families Village" is a village by the sea. The coastal residents mostly take "salt drying boards" as their main business, and farming as a byproduct. Salt drying boards are first used to filter seawater into clear dew, then the clear dew is placed on wooden salt boards, and the salt boards are placed on "mounds" to be dried in the sun. After a considerable period, it becomes the table salt we use every day. As for the fields there, because they are close to the beach, the soil is not very fertile, and there is often the danger of seawater flooding, so although they generally work hard to cultivate, the harvest is always limited. Therefore, their lives mostly depend on the income from salt drying, and what they get from farming is only used to supplement it. Of course, they also hope for a bountiful harvest.

Salt drying and farming are of course both laborious occupations, and they cannot be slackened off at all. According to the general custom in China, men take sole responsibility for this, and women are only in a supporting position. However, in this "Five Mounds Six Families Village," it is exactly the opposite. Women take responsibility for all the heavy work, and men only follow them to clean up all the trivial and easy tasks. Therefore, the nearby residents gave them these two strange sayings under strange eyes: "Five Mounds Six Families Village, wives support men"; and when they are free from work, the women carry the dried salt to sell in other places, and the men, on the other hand, stay at home and gamble with cards for entertainment. Therefore, there is also the saying "women sell salt, men gamble with cards."

Therefore, the women in the "Five Mounds Six Families Village" are mostly rough, dark, strong, and big-footed, meeting the aesthetic conditions of modern times.

Although this kind of life is too deformed, we cannot but give considerable praise to their perseverance and determination to "earn their own living," and recognize that this is what modern liberated women should emulate.

Impression of Wen Kegang's Calligraphy Exhibition 147

— Bai Gong

I have long heard that Mr. Wen Yiru of Lingnan is devoted to calligraphy, and he has studied the inscriptions on bronzes, tripods, Qin and Han stone tablets, as well as the calligraphy of various masters since the Jin and Tang dynasties. Every time he copies them, the spirit and charm are very lifelike, which is highly praised by contemporary scholars. Yesterday, I visited the calligraphy and painting exhibition jointly held by Mr. Wen and Mr. Wu Gonghu at the Lake Society on Guizhou Road. I truly felt that the walls were full of exquisite works, and it was too beautiful to describe. Just talking about the various copied works, Zheng Yuan said that his copy of "Stone Gate Ode" captured the essence of the original. Pan Feisheng (deceased) said that his spirit was wonderfully in tune with the ancients. Ye Gongchuo said that his copy of "Zhang Qian's Memorial Stele" uniquely captured its composure. Tan Zekai said that he deeply understood the essence of it. Zhou Zhenlin said that his copy of "Jing Jun Stele" was extremely commendable and worthy of admiration. Pan Feisheng said that his copy was exceptionally refined and made people yearn for it. Ye Gongchuo said that his copy of "Fragmentary Han Tablet" was described by people in the past as "like iron sinking into jade," which is the best description. I also say the same about this copy. Zheng Yuan said that his copy of "Zhong Wang's Running Script and Regular Script" corrected the vulgarity and directly entered the room of the Jin people. Zheng Yuan said that his copy of "Wang Xianzhi's Post" not only resembled the shape but also captured the spirit. Chuan Shaoyan said that he deeply understood the spirit of the Great Order. Wang Xishen said that he transcended the outward form and captured the essence. Huang Binhong and Fu Shaoyan both said that his copy of "Han and Jin Cursive Script" captured the spirit. Yang Shukan said that his copy of "Wang Xizhi's True Writings," especially the "Mid-Autumn Post," was extremely lifelike. It can be said that he has a high talent and has put in the deepest effort. It cannot be compared to the copies of his contemporaries. I can only admire him. The gentlemen are all famous figures of the same era, and they have never had the habit of self-promotion, but they highly praised Mr. Wen's calligraphy, which shows the depth of his attainments. Mr. Wen's exhibition is actually set up to help disaster victims. I secretly hope that those who are interested in this art and want to feast their eyes and show their elegance should not miss this good opportunity.

Misty Records of the Imperial Incense 148

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

"Because we can't wait until that time, the Emperor has to rush back to Beijing to preside over the grand ceremony of worshiping the ancestral temple!"

While the Empress Dowager was sighing like this, Guangxu and I were also standing beside her. When he heard the last sentence, he couldn't help but shrug his shoulders slightly, as if he was very reluctant to listen. Indeed, the views of this prisoner-like Emperor were quite good! He has always opposed the boring acts of burning incense to worship Buddha and offering sacrifices to Heaven and ancestors! He especially disagreed with spending a lot of energy, time, and money on ceremonies to commemorate or pay tribute to those who have already died. This kind of thinking was truly unique among the nobles at that time! This day, after work, he found a chance when no one was watching and quietly said to me:

"Since we are in charge of the affairs of a country, we cannot spend most of our time on such meaningless sacrifices... We should shift our eyes and use all our strength to build a strong army and navy, which is what we should do. Remember the other day when we went to visit Fox Immortal Pagoda together, the Old Buddha had a lesson for you, you probably haven't forgotten it, right? You might as well honestly tell me, can you really believe it?"

What he was referring to was that the other day, I accidentally showed distrust of the Green Fox Immortal in front of the Empress Dowager in the Fox Immortal Pagoda, which led to the Empress Dowager's rebuke. In fact, this matter has left a deep mark on my nerves, how could I forget it?

"That thing? The Old Buddha just told me to kowtow a few times!" (232)

Odds and Ends

Suzhou's Calligraphy and Painting Exhibition 149

— Zhu [unclear character]

Suzhou is a good place where cultural relics gather. Besides the gentle, water-like women, calligraphy and painting masters have also emerged from generation to generation, decorating the paradise-like Suzhou with a civilized atmosphere. Recently, the Suzhou calligraphy and painting groups, besides the Zheng Society exhibiting in Nanjing, also have a "Suzhou Calligraphy and Painting Society." The people in charge of the society, such as Mr. Chen Jia'an, Wu Daiqiu, Gu Moyi, Fan Shaoyun, Liu Junran, and Zhang Yisheng, are all famous painters who are famous in Suzhou and Shanghai... This time, each of them has produced wonderful works to hold a painting exhibition in Shanghai, adding a scene of brocade and flowers to the cold and year-end Shanghai art world. It is truly not only a grand event in the art world but also a feast for people's eyes.

The Suzhou Calligraphy and Painting Society has been preparing for this exhibition in Shanghai for a long time. In order for the people of Suzhou to appreciate it, an exhibition was held in Suzhou in the middle of last month. The opening days were truly crowded with viewers, who unanimously praised it. Half of the works in the exhibition were booked. Therefore, the people in charge deeply felt that these paintings were not enough. After the closing, the painters all worked hard to produce more, but because the mounting took time and the rain continued, it was not until recently that the weather turned sunny, and the painters' works were all mounted. Therefore, it was decided to hold the exhibition at Tianyi Society on Sanma Road from the 26th.

In the society's exhibition paintings, the works of painters Chen Jia'an and Liu Junran are displayed the most. Mr. Jia'an's paintings are famous throughout the north and south of the Yangtze River. His brushstrokes are so elegant, but the flowers, birds, and feathers he writes are both in shape and spirit. This time, he produced more than twenty works, with flowers, birds, landscapes, and everything. In one painting, there are chicks under the fence, flowers all over the frame, grass like a carpet, and several yellow chicks pecking for food, as if they are about to jump off the paper. Points to Note When Using Electrolytic Capacitors 150

— Yong Yan

There are two kinds of commonly used large capacitors, one is paper capacitors, and the other is electrolytic capacitors. Among these two, the latter is easily damaged, but the price is low and it takes up very little space. Therefore, it is especially popular recently. It can be said that most of the large capacitors in imported radios are electrolytic. However, electrolytic capacitors can also be very durable if used legally. The following are some points to note when using them:

1. Withstand Voltage Strength Each electrolytic capacitor has a specified withstand voltage strength. It is absolutely forbidden to exceed it during use, otherwise the internal insulation material will be broken down and a short circuit will occur. It is safer to reduce the quantity than to use it. The withstand voltage strength of the filter capacitor in the filter circuit of an AC radio should be at least 1.4 times the secondary high voltage of its power transformer. For example, for an electrolytic capacitor with a specified voltage of 500 volts, the secondary voltage should not exceed 350 volts. (350 multiplied by 1.4 is 490, which is about 500 volts.)

2. There are two types of electrolytic capacitors: dry and wet. Wet ones have more leakage, but they can withstand occasional voltage increases in the circuit. The latter will be damaged once the voltage is high. Therefore, wet electrolytic capacitors should be used in places where the voltage changes frequently, which is safer.

3. Electrolytic capacitors have two wiring heads, which have positive and negative poles. It is absolutely forbidden to make mistakes when wiring, otherwise it will be damaged immediately.

4. After electrolytic capacitors are left unused, the internal insulation will gradually disappear. Before reusing them, they should be used under low voltage for a few minutes, so that the lost insulation can be regenerated by itself; it is safe to use.

5. Electrolytic capacitors should not be placed in high temperatures, because high temperatures may shorten their lifespan.

Quick Verification Method for Short Circuit of Power Transformer 151

— Li Yuanqing

Once a short circuit (Short Circuit) occurs in the coil of the power transformer, if you do not have a precision meter at hand, it is difficult to measure and verify it for a while. The method described in this article does not require specialized instruments and complicated procedures, and can find out the location of the coil short circuit for you in a very short time.

As shown in the figure, T is the power transformer and L is the commonly used light bulb. During measurement and verification, first take out all the vacuum tubes in the radio completely, and then turn on the switch SW. At this time, carefully observe the light bulb L as follows:

(1) No light at all: It proves that the secondary coils are all intact, and the design of the transformer is also very good.

(2) Red light: It proves that a short circuit has occurred in the low-voltage secondary coil, or a small part of the high-voltage secondary coil has a short circuit. (If there is very dim light, this is the inevitable loss of ordinary transformers, such as eddy current loss (Eddycurrent Loss), etc., and it is not a short circuit of the secondary coil, so be careful.

(3) White light: It proves that a short circuit has occurred in the high-voltage secondary coil.

(4) Sometimes bright and sometimes dim: A short circuit is about to occur in the secondary coil.

If a short circuit occurs in the primary coil, the secondary coils will immediately exceed the normal value, which is easy to observe. If there is a broken line or touching line in each coil, it is even easier to measure and verify it with a voltmeter or stethoscope in series with a battery. This article is to save space, so it is omitted here.

Discussion on Using High-Power Tubes to Make Single-Tube Machines 152

— Wu Zipei

Reading the article "Improvement of Using High-Power Vacuum Tubes for Detection" by KMK in the 98th issue can reduce distortion and stabilize the tone, which can be used as a reference for general enthusiasts.

The amplification coefficient of high-power tubes is very large. When used for detection, the volume is no less than that of ordinary two-tube machines; however, the power consumption is extremely large. For example, for the battery-type 33, the filament voltage needs 2V and the current needs 0.26A, a total of 0.52W. A small 25A battery needs to be charged after 40 hours of use; and the B voltage needs at least 45V to 90V, and the screen heat and grid heat need a total of 17.5MA. The B battery sold on the market is less than three amperes. It must be replaced with a new battery after a maximum of 200 hours of use. The monthly cost is about three times more expensive than energy-saving tubes; If 42 or 2A5A are powered from AC power and B power is used with dry batteries, the monthly cost will be four times more expensive than energy-saving tubes. If all AC power is used, the monthly maintenance cost is lower, but the installation cost is more expensive, which is not very cost-effective.

In summary, using high-power tubes for detection is better than energy-saving tubes in terms of effectiveness, but the monthly cost is also considerable.

The circuit of MKK uses three or four lines, and it is unquestionable to use a variable capacitor to adjust the screen circuit. However, if it is changed to the Hartley connection method, that is, the secondary circuit is connected to the screen circuit, and the screen current is still adjusted by a variable capacitor, the feedback force can be more stable, and the wiring is more convenient and the effectiveness is reliable.

The resistance of the grid heat should be larger for radio stations with shorter wavelengths, and smaller for radio stations with longer wavelengths; the adjustable resistance can be adjusted to the most pleasing point; and a small-capacity fixed capacitor is connected across both ends of the headphones or speakers, then the sound quality can be improved a lot.

When using high-power tubes or five heat tubes, the most important thing to pay attention to is: do not turn on the power when the screen circuit is not connected, otherwise the grid heat will be damaged, and the effectiveness will be 90% or 80% reduced when it is used later.

I have previously disassembled and assembled 2A5, 33, 58, and 42 several times, and I am convinced that the effectiveness is not bad, so I specifically bring it up to inform the enthusiasts.

Continuing the Method of Protecting Diaphragms 153

— Feng Weiqiao

After reading Mr. A Feng's method of protecting diaphragms in the 98th issue of this publication, I couldn't help but recall my own sound methods for properly protecting diaphragms. As earpieces are necessary components of ordinary radios, the proper protection of diaphragms is extremely important.

For newly purchased earpieces, one should simultaneously purchase mica sheets (commonly known as thousand-layer paper) from wireless radio materials shops or hardware stores. One sheet can be divided into two pieces, costing only five or six copper coins. Cut the mica sheets to the same size as the diaphragm, and glue them around the edges to form a single sheet. After the glue dries, screw it into the earpiece cover. This will not only permanently ensure that the diaphragm will not rust or become contaminated, but also increase sound transmission efficiency. Readers may wish to try it.

If you find that the diaphragm has already rusted, first carefully scrape off the rust with a small knife or sandpaper, then wipe it clean with cotton dipped in methylated spirits. After drying, apply pencil lead to the rusted area to prevent further rusting.

Varieties of Detection 154

— Si Lian

The radio waves emitted by transmitters have extremely high frequencies that cannot be heard by the human ear. Therefore, a detector must be used to rectify them into audio frequencies. The detectors currently used on the market can be divided into two types: crystal detectors and vacuum tube detectors. Crystal detectors lack selectivity and amplification capability, which is their only drawback. However, because they are cheap to install and inexpensive, people are happy to use them. Vacuum tube detectors are more widely used, and thus come in more varieties, roughly divided into five types: grid leak detection (Grid leak and Condenser detector), grid bias detection (Gridbias detector), also known as plate detection, half-wave detection (Half Wave detector), full-wave detection (Full Wave detector), and push-pull detection or Class B detection (Push Pull detector or class B detector). The five types of detection are described below:

(1) Grid Leak Detection || This type of detection is composed of a high-value resistor and a capacitor, as shown in Figure 1. R is a 2-megohm high resistance, and C is a 0.00025-microfarad fixed capacitor. Its function is that R allows the grid to obtain a considerable negative voltage, while C allows high-frequency waves to easily pass through to the grid. RFC blocks high-frequency waves from flowing into the audio frequency section. C is a bypass capacitor with a capacitance of 0.00025 microfarads, whose function is to allow high-frequency waves to flow back to their original location. Grid leak detection is the most widely used on the current market because of its excellent sensitivity, surpassing other types of detection, and also has good selectivity. However, the plate voltage should not be too high, because the voltage that the grid receives is limited. Too high will easily cause distortion when emitting sound, and too low will not cause oscillation. Moreover, after the resonant point, a "whistling" sound that is most annoying to people will occur in the speaker or earpiece. It is acceptable for oneself to hear it, but nearby radios are also disturbed. Therefore, this type of detection has been banned in European and American countries.

(2) Plate Detection || When using grid bias detection, the voltage that its grid should obtain usually depends on the voltage used by the plate. For example, if a #30 vacuum tube is used for plate detection, and its B voltage is 90 volts, then the C voltage should be 4.5 volts. If the B voltage is 135 volts, then the C voltage also needs to be increased to 9 volts. The sensitivity of this type of detection is inferior to that of grid leak detection, but the oscillation is more stable, and the adjustment is simpler. Therefore, it is not commonly used in DC radios except for superheterodyne or multi-tube tuned radio frequency amplification.

In AC machines, this type of detection is the most common. Its power supply does not use a C battery, but uses a C-battery substitute. This C-battery substitute is composed of a resistor and a fixed capacitor. Vacuum tubes with cathodes are connected to the cathode, as shown in Figure 2. R is a bleeder resistor, and C is a fixed capacitor. Vacuum tubes without cathodes, such as #47, are connected to the center tap, but they are not commonly used for detection, as they easily cause AC hum.

(3) Half-Wave Detection. Figure 3 shows the half-wave detection circuit. V is a dual-grid triode, such as #55, #75, #85, 2A6, 6A6 vacuum tubes, or a dual-grid pentode is used for half-wave detection (such as #2B7, #6B7). The dual-grid portion is able to detect entirely due to its unidirectional nature, thus it can rectify radio waves. This type of detection is often used as the second stage of detection in superheterodyne radios, while the triode portion is used for amplification or automatic volume control.

Small Experiences 158

— Jian Qin

▲ Earpiece Jack Wei Wei

Sometimes, in order to check whether the circuit of the detection stage or a certain low-frequency amplification stage is intact, or for the sake of good listening etiquette, we want to use an earpiece to test the sound on a multi-tube DC radio. However, connecting and disconnecting the wires is very troublesome. To avoid this trouble, we can conveniently use an old vacuum tube base, with two binding posts connected next to it. These two binding posts are prepared for connecting the earpiece terminals. The wiring is as shown in diagram A. This is a very convenient earpiece jack. When using it, just plug it into the tube socket of any low-frequency amplification tube (the original amplification tube is of course removed). In other words, this jack is used to replace the original amplification tube, but it is only not suitable for replacing push-pull amplification tubes.

▲ Shortwave Plug-in Coil Tube

We often use old vacuum tube bases for shortwave plug-in coil tubes for economic reasons. However, when the number of coil turns is large, the space seems too narrow. We always want to extend the tube base. Usually, thick paper is used to circle the tube base, but this method has the disadvantage of unevenness. The best way is to make the base and the thick paper the same height, as shown in diagram B. First, circle a layer of thick paper in the tube base as the inner layer, and then paste another layer of thick paper outside the inner layer (if there is a ready-made battery case whose circumference is suitable for the tube base, then it can be placed on the inner layer). In this way, there is no unevenness between the thick paper and the bakelite base, and it becomes a cheap and high-quality plug-in coil tube.

▲ High-Frequency Choke

I believe that most people who play with radios know that when capacitors are connected in series, their capacitance is reduced. Similarly, we can apply this to the winding method of high-impedance coils. Therefore, commercially available products all use a segmented winding method, because this can reduce capacitance. When we wind our own high-impedance coils, we should also follow this winding method in order to obtain higher efficiency. For convenience, two wooden thread spools can be combined, as shown in diagram C. Wind about 500 turns of #36 enameled wire on this, each spool. If you want to be more precise, then each wooden spool can be separated into two sections with wood or thick paper that has been permeated with wax. Note that there is no need to seek neatness when winding, just wind it randomly, because this can reduce the distributed capacitance between the coils. When you connect it into the circuit, you will know that this high-impedance coil has a higher efficiency than ordinary ones.

▲ Dead Spots in Shortwave

In shortwave radios, sometimes dead spots are found. This is probably because the coupling is too tight. To avoid these dead spots, we can wind three turns of #18 enameled wire on the tube socket of the plug-in coil, with one end not connected and the other end connected to the antenna. This is equivalent to connecting an antenna compensation capacitor. However, the grid coil should be wound on the lower part of the plug-in tube, and the direction of the three coils should be consistent, otherwise it will not be effective.

Ministry of Education Order: First Semester, Second Term 174

High School Normal Military Training

April 10th to July 10th

Ordinary Subjects to End Early

(Nanjing, 25th) The Ministry of Education issued an order to the Education Bureaus of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Fujian, Jiangxi, Hubei, Hunan, Hebei, Henan, Shandong, and Shanxi provinces, as well as the Social Affairs Bureau of Beijing and Tianjin cities, and the Education Bureaus of Shanghai and Qingdao cities, stating that concentrated military training should be held in the second semester of the first academic year, according to Article 13 of the revised military education program. It was also clearly stipulated that the concentrated training time for high schools and equivalent schools should be from April 11th to July 10th, and all were ordered to comply. Considering that the second academic year is about to begin, all high school and normal school students who should receive concentrated military training should complete all ordinary subjects before the stipulated time, so as to participate in the concentrated training. You are ordered to instruct all high schools and normal schools under your jurisdiction to comply accordingly.

French Mathematical Authority Hadamard to Lecture in China 178

▲ Tsinghua and Sino-French Cultural Foundation Jointly Hire

丨 Hadamard Responds by Telegraph that He Will Come to Beijing This Spring

The Department of Mathematics of National Tsinghua University heard that the great French mathematician Hadamard (J. Hadamard) intends to come to the East, so it consulted with the school authorities and the Sino-French Education and Culture Foundation to jointly hire Hadamard to lecture in China for half a year. First, Xiong Didi, the head of the department, wrote to Hadamard to discuss the matter. After both organizations agreed, Tsinghua formally sent a letter of engagement. Last month, Hadamard replied to Xiong, stating that he could not spare time this year due to hosting the Geneva academic conference, but he could come in March of this year, and that remuneration was not a concern. Yesterday, Hadamard telegraphed the school authorities to formally accept the engagement. It is reported that Hadamard is a leading mathematical authority of the contemporary era, on par with Borel, with extensive knowledge and rich contributions. He has solved many difficult problems and pioneered many paths in mathematics, and has published nearly 300 papers, many of which have become models. Hadamard's visit will undoubtedly have a profound impact on academic research in our country.

Ministry of Education Commissioners and Supervisors Inspect Education 180

Inspection of Education in Fujian, Guangdong, and Guangxi Provinces

In order to understand the situation of specialized schools and above and vocational education in Fujian, Guangdong, and Guangxi provinces, the Ministry of Education specially dispatched Sun Guofeng, a commissioner of the Ministry, and Dai Xia, a supervisor, to inspect. Sun and Dai went south in November of last year after receiving the order, and after completing the inspection in the provinces of Fujian, Guangdong, and Guangxi, they returned to Beijing yesterday to report. When reporters visited them and inquired about the inspection process, they said that after receiving the Ministry order on November 16th last year, Supervisor Dai went to Shanghai on the 18th to prepare ships, and Commissioner Sun went to Shanghai on the 20th. They went south on the same ship on the 22nd and arrived in Xiamen on the 24th. They immediately went to Xiamen University to inspect the school's administration. The next day was Sunday. On the 26th and 27th, they inspected the teaching and equipment conditions of the school's various colleges. On the 28th, they inspected the Fujian Provincial Xiamen Vocational School. On the 29th, they took a ship to Fuzhou and arrived the next night. On December 1st, they discussed the Xiamen University subsidy with the Fujian Provincial Government. The 2nd was Sunday, and they visited the Fujian Public Education Science Museum and the private Hui'er Orphanage. On the 3rd, they inspected the private Fujian Union College. On the morning of the 4th, they inspected the private Hwa Nan Women's College of Arts and Sciences, and in the afternoon, they inspected the private Fujian College. On the 5th, they inspected the Fujian Provincial Fuzhou Industrial and Vocational Schools and the Senior Agricultural Vocational School. On the 6th, they took a ship back to Xiamen and transferred to Hong Kong, arriving on the 9th. On the 10th, they went to Guangzhou and arrived on the 11th. On the 12th, they visited Chairman Lin of the Guangdong Provincial Government and the Director of the Education Department to discuss and determine the inspection procedures. On the 13th, they inspected the administration of the main campus of National Sun Yat-sen University and the teaching and equipment conditions of the Colleges of Arts and Sciences. On the morning of the 14th, they inspected the new campus of the school, the teaching and equipment of the Colleges of Law and Engineering, and in the afternoon, they inspected the College of Agriculture and the agricultural and forestry fields. On the 15th, they inspected the private Guangdong National University. The 16th was Sunday, and they inspected the new campus of the Provincial Xiangqin University in Shiliugang. On the 17th, they inspected the school. That evening, Pang Jingzhou, the medical inspector sent by the Ministry of Education, arrived in Guangzhou, so the inspection procedures were revised. On the 18th, they inspected the private Lingnan University. On the morning of the 19th, they inspected the private Xia Ge Medical College, and in the afternoon, they inspected the private Guangzhou Law College. On the morning of the 20th, they inspected the private Guangdong Guanghua Medical College, and in the afternoon, they inspected the National Guangdong Academy of Law and Science. On the morning of the 21st, they inspected the private Guangzhou University, and in the afternoon, they inspected the Provincial First Vocational School. On the morning of the 22nd, they inspected the Guangzhou Municipal Third Vocational School, and in the afternoon, they inspected the private Zhongkai School of Agriculture and Engineering in Guangzhou Province. The 23rd was Sunday. They were invited by President Zou of Sun Yat-sen University to visit Luogang Cave and inspect the school's agricultural and forestry branch fields. On the morning of the 24th, they inspected the Guangzhou Municipal First Vocational School, and in the afternoon, they inspected the Second Vocational School. On the 25th, they visited Commander-in-Chief Li of Guangxi at his private residence in Dongshan, Guangzhou. On the 26th, they took a car to Sanshui and transferred to another ship, arriving in Wuzhou on the 27th. On the 28th, they inspected the teaching and equipment conditions of the Colleges of Science and Engineering of Guangxi University. On the 29th, they inspected the school's College of Agriculture and the administration of all departments of the school. The 30th was Sunday. The next day, they inspected the vocational subjects of the Provincial Wuzhou Girls' High School. On New Year's Day this year, they took a long-distance bus to Nanning and arrived on the 2nd. On the 3rd, they visited Vice Commander Bai. On the 4th, they inspected the Provincial Medical College Chemical Research Institute and the Guangxi Popular Basic Education Research Institute. On the 5th, they took a car to Guilin and arrived on the 6th in Liangfeng. On the 7th, they inspected the Provincial Normal College. From the 8th to Guilin, they inspected the Guilin County Work-Study School. On the 9th, they took a long-distance bus, passing through Liuzhou, Binyang, and Guixian, and arrived in Wuzhou on the evening of the 11th. On the 12th, they took a ship and arrived in Hong Kong the next night. On the evening of the 15th, they boarded a ship and returned to Shanghai on the 18th. On the 19th, they discussed the inspection of various medical colleges in South China with medical inspector Pang Jingzhou. The 20th was Sunday. On the 21st and 22nd, they sorted out the inspection materials. On the evening of the 23rd, they returned to Beijing and reported the inspection process to the Vice Ministers of the Ministry of Education on the 24th. As for the scope of this inspection, in addition to special matters that need to be specially inspected in each school, such as (1) the organization of school administration and the distribution of staff, (2) the source and expenditure of funds and the public disclosure methods, accounting methods, (3) the current status of the establishment of departments, (4) the qualifications of teachers, the proportion of full-time and part-time teachers, and the standards of teaching and salary, (5) the diligence of students in attending classes and self-study and the situation of academic performance, (6) the location and area of the school buildings and the construction matching the number and capacity of classrooms, and the setting of other rooms, museums, and venues, (7) the equipment of books, instruments, specimens, medicines, and the mechanical tools needed for practice or research, (8) the content of courses and teaching materials, teaching methods and progress, the examination and research of achievements and research experience, and the guidance of graduation theses, (9) the training policy, counseling methods, and the rectification of discipline and the examination of conduct, (10) the equipment of physical education, military training, hygiene, and other facilities, etc., are all included in the items to be inspected. It is also heard that the members are rushing to prepare the inspection report, and it will be submitted to the Vice Ministers of the Ministry of Education for review as soon as the draft is completed.

Report of the Shanghai Municipal Council Public Library 181

According to the report of the director of the Shanghai Municipal Council Public Library for the past year, the number of long-term subscribers that year was 68 Chinese and 556 foreigners, totaling 624, an increase of 24 compared with 1933. The number of books borrowed was 56,571 novels, 11,742 general books, and 934 children's books, totaling 69,247, an increase of 7,521 compared to the previous year. Among them, the circulation of novels increased by only 5%, while the circulation of non-fiction books increased by 45%.

The book purchase fee that year was 4,060 yuan. In addition, a set of the Encyclopedia Britannica and 40 books on economic issues were purchased, with another 1,000 yuan spent. A total of 793 new books were purchased, including 370 novels, 345 non-fiction books, and 80 children's books, as well as several maps and dictionaries. A complete set of Chinese art magazines was also purchased for the needs of the reference section. In addition, 39 books were donated from outside the library. Classification and cataloging are still in progress. The novel section has been completed, and other books will be processed in succession. A total of 1,289 books were rebound. In terms of newspapers and magazines, seven new magazines and four daily newspapers were added this year, including one Chinese newspaper, the Xinwenbao, and one English newspaper, the Continental Daily. In order to facilitate readers and rectify order, a cloakroom was added to the library in August to allow readers to store their belongings. In order to facilitate readers to borrow books, a telephone was installed.

Pudong Middle School has been on the right track in recent years, and students are studying with peace of mind. Commercial News

Financial Foreign Exchange Seems Slightly Tighter 187

Gold Standard Price Long Stagnant, Yesterday a Slight Rebound

丨Steady Rise of One Yuan and Three Jiao丨

The gold market rebounded after yesterday's decline, resulting in a steady outcome, mainly due to banks' lack of selling interest. The exchange rate market tended to tighten, stimulating Hua merchants and the Dalian gang to cover their short positions. However, due to HSBC and Sassoon taking the opportunity to sell high, it ultimately became mediocre. Initially, overseas silver markets in both the UK and the US were flat. The London forward silver price remained unchanged, exchange rates slightly contracted, and the French franc weakened further. As a result, the London spot gold price fell by nine and a half pence. Over-the-counter forward transactions opened, retreating to around eight yuan, then surged to over nine yuan as bargain hunters flooded in. The Central Bank's official exchange rates were announced, with both the UK and the US remaining flat, and the customs gold unit falling by 1 fen and 1 li. The gold standard price retreated to 980 yuan and 3 jiao. The morning opened with lower prices, and although slightly weak after the opening, it rose to over sixty yuan due to banks' lack of selling interest and the tightening exchange rate market, stimulating buying sentiment. Despite fluctuations, it was soon learned that the official exchange rates of HSBC for both British and American currencies remained unchanged. Although HSBC and Chase Manhattan had supply, the buying interest of banks turned strong, the process tightened, and the gold market also sought more than it supplied. Major players aggressively covered their short positions, gradually rising. The Silver Equalization Tax was announced, remaining unchanged. A speculator named Luo suddenly came to cover his short position, at which time it appeared quite firm. Later, due to some selling by major players, but speculator Luo continued to buy, and the Dalian gang aggressively covered Dalian positions, so the exchange rate market remained tight. Although it fell, it was still easy to rebound. Later, banks took the opportunity to sell high, and Sassoon also slightly supplied, and the exchange rate market gradually stabilized. The buying sentiment in the market slightly subsided, and the supply side became active from time to time. Transactions had decreased, gradually moving downstream, once approaching sixty yuan. At noon, the market situation was mediocre, with a soft trend. The after-market turned from flat to stable, with fewer transactions but strong buying sentiment. Banks still had supply, and prices slightly decreased after the high. The Indian silver market initially reported fluctuations, presenting a wavering situation. After entering the market, major players aggressively sold, and retail investors panicked, once falling to sixty yuan. However, although Sassoon supplied in the exchange rate market, there was no special change. After the price dropped, there were many who bought to cover their positions. The Indian silver market's second report of a decline gradually rebounded, but the transactions were light, and the market situation was boring. Finally, the overall trend was mediocre, with limited ups and downs. The swap premium had risen to 9 yuan and 8 jiao, which was due to the forced posting by many parties during the settlement period. The day's market situation is recorded below.

The morning opening was 958 yuan and 9 jiao, a slight decrease of 7 jiao compared to the previous close. Fuchang and others sold slightly, retreating to 8 yuan and 2 jiao. Chunyuan, Yongheng, Yu Yongli, Richang, Fuyu, Yongda, Kang Qian, Changxiang, Jiarun, Fuyu, etc. bought to cover their positions at low prices, rising to over sixty yuan. Yuanchang, Yongyi, Feng Yongfu, and Yongheng Yu sold off, retreating to around 59 yuan and 5 jiao. It was learned in advance that HSBC's official exchange rate remained unchanged. The US dollar for March at 81.25 was difficult to settle. Fuyu, Yongfu Yu, Zhaofeng, Changyuan, Maoyongchangda, etc. bought strips, rising to sixty-two yuan. HSBC sold spot shillings at 4.375, and Dafayongju, Dayongde, Yifengyongqianlai sold off, retreating to one yuan. However, due to the bank's need for shillings at 5 pence in May, people's hearts were still strong. Hengyu, Yongli, Fuyu, Yongding, Changda, Decheng, Tongyu, Runyu, Qing Yongyi, Feng Yonghui, Xiangyuan, Maoyong, etc. successively bought strips, gradually rising. Although there was some struggle in the middle due to HSBC selling bills of exchange, and Dafayongyi Yu had some supply, it still rose to 4 yuan and 4 jiao. The Silver Equalization Tax was announced, remaining unchanged. Huabi and others settled the US dollar for March at 6.25 yuan.
